\section{Clifford Closure of the TECT Reduced Symbol}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The reduced Branch B symbol obtained from the Bloch projection is

\[
H_B(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
\]

This acts on the two–component tangent fermion.
However, the Bloch shell contains two opposite valleys,
so the true low–energy Hilbert space is

\[
\mathcal H_{low}
=
\mathbb C^2_{int}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{valley}.
\]

This allows the construction of a \(4\times4\) Clifford carrier.

---

\subsection{1. Valley doubling}

Define valley basis

\[
|+\rangle,\quad |-\rangle .
\]

Introduce Pauli matrices

\[
\tau_i
\]

acting in valley space.

The tangent Pauli matrices

\[
\sigma_i
\]

act in the internal sector.

---

\subsection{2. Candidate Clifford generators}

Define

\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes\sigma^1
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes\sigma^2
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes\mathbf1
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{3. Clifford algebra check}

Compute

\[
(\Gamma^1)^2
=
(\tau^1)^2\otimes(\sigma^1)^2
=
\mathbf1_4
\]

Similarly

\[
(\Gamma^2)^2=\mathbf1_4
\]

\[
(\Gamma^3)^2=\mathbf1_4
\]

Now compute anticommutators.

First

\[
\Gamma^1\Gamma^2
=
(\tau^1\tau^1)\otimes(\sigma^1\sigma^2)
=
\mathbf1\otimes i\sigma^3
\]

\[
\Gamma^2\Gamma^1
=
\mathbf1\otimes(-i\sigma^3)
\]

Therefore

\[
\{\Gamma^1,\Gamma^2\}=0
\]

Next

\[
\Gamma^1\Gamma^3
=
(\tau^1\tau^3)\otimes\sigma^1
=
i\tau^2\otimes\sigma^1
\]

\[
\Gamma^3\Gamma^1
=
(-i\tau^2)\otimes\sigma^1
\]

Thus

\[
\{\Gamma^1,\Gamma^3\}=0
\]

Similarly

\[
\{\Gamma^2,\Gamma^3\}=0
\]

Hence

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}
=
2\delta^{ij}\mathbf1_4
}
\end{equation}

which is the Clifford algebra \(Cl(3)\).

---

\subsection{4. Dirac Hamiltonian}

The canonical Dirac Hamiltonian is therefore

\begin{equation}
H_D
=
v_\perp p_1\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\Gamma^3 .
\end{equation}

Explicitly

\[
H_D
=
v_\perp p_1(\tau^1\otimes\sigma^1)
+
v_\perp p_2(\tau^1\otimes\sigma^2)
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf1).
\]

---

\subsection{5. Spectrum}

Squaring gives

\[
H_D^2
=
(v_\perp^2p_1^2+v_\perp^2p_2^2+v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2)\mathbf1_4
\]

so the dispersion is

\[
E(p)
=
\pm\sqrt{
v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2)
}.
\]

Thus the TECT reduced symbol is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

\section{Dirac Emergence in TECT}

The Bloch shell produces two opposite valleys,
so the low–energy Hilbert space is

\[
\mathcal H_{low}
=
\mathbb C^2_{int}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{valley}.
\]

Define

\[
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes\sigma^1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes\sigma^2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes\mathbf1.
\]

These satisfy

\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}
=
2\delta^{ij}\mathbf1_4 .
\]

Therefore the reduced Hamiltonian

\[
H_B(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
\]

embeds into the Dirac Hamiltonian

\[
H_D
=
v_\perp p_1\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\Gamma^3 .
\]

Thus the TECT infrared fermion is a massless Dirac fermion.

\section{Honest Clifford-Closure Statement for the Current TECT Reduced Operator}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At the current stage, the reduced infrared operator is already fixed at the theorem level as a nondegenerate first-order graded operator.
What can be proved now is the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact reduced Branch-B operator is an anisotropic massless Dirac-type operator;
\item there is a canonical \(4\times4\) Clifford carrier compatible with the opposite-valley doubled sector;
\item if the actual microscopic projected matrices close on that carrier, then the reduced PDE is unitarily equivalent to the standard massless Dirac equation;
\item the remaining open part is the final microscopic Bloch calibration of the projected coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{1. Exact reduced \(2\times 2\) symbol}

The exact reduced low-energy symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_reduced_current}
\end{equation}
Its nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:A1_nondeg_current}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
v_\perp:=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}.
\label{eq:vperp_def_current}
\end{equation}
After a constant transverse rotation in the \((p_1,p_2)\)-plane and an associated spinor basis rotation, \eqref{eq:A1_reduced_current} is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
A_1'(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_\perp\,(p_1'\sigma_1+p_2'\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_canonical_current}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced PDE is already of exact anisotropic massless Weyl/Dirac-type.

\subsection{2. Dispersion and principal cone}

Using the Pauli algebra
\[
\sigma_i\sigma_j+\sigma_j\sigma_i=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_2,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
A_1'(p)^2
=
\bigl(
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1'^2+p_2'^2)
\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:A1_square_current}
\end{equation}
Therefore the exact reduced dispersion is
\begin{equation}
E(p)=\pm\sqrt{\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp'^2}.
\label{eq:dispersion_current}
\end{equation}
This is an anisotropic massless cone.

\subsection{3. Opposite-valley doubling and the \(4\times4\) carrier}

Assume the standard opposite-valley pairing already isolated in the reduced theorem:
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p).
\]
Then the doubled low-energy carrier is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{low}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:Hlow_def_current}
\end{equation}
Let \(\tau_i\) act on the valley factor and \(\sigma_i\) act on the internal two-band factor.

Define the three \(4\times4\) matrices
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1:=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2:=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Gamma_choice_current}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
(\Gamma^1)^2=(\Gamma^2)^2=(\Gamma^3)^2=\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:Gamma_sq_current}
\end{equation}
Moreover,
\begin{align}
\Gamma^1\Gamma^2+\Gamma^2\Gamma^1
&=
(\tau_x\tau_x)\otimes(\sigma_1\sigma_2+\sigma_2\sigma_1)=0,
\\
\Gamma^1\Gamma^3+\Gamma^3\Gamma^1
&=
(\tau_x\tau_z+\tau_z\tau_x)\otimes \sigma_1 =0,
\\
\Gamma^2\Gamma^3+\Gamma^3\Gamma^2
&=
(\tau_x\tau_z+\tau_z\tau_x)\otimes \sigma_2 =0.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
}
\label{eq:Clifford_current}
\end{equation}
So the doubled carrier supports a genuine \(Cl(3)\) Clifford algebra.

\subsection{4. Canonical \(4\times4\) doubled Hamiltonian}

On this carrier, define
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)
=
v_\perp p_1'\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2'\Gamma^2
+
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3.
\label{eq:HD_current}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Clifford_current},
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)^2
=
\bigl(
v_\perp^2 p_1'^2
+
v_\perp^2 p_2'^2
+
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
\bigr)\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:HD_square_current}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_D(p))
=
\pm
\sqrt{\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp'^2},
\label{eq:HD_spec_current}
\end{equation}
which agrees with the reduced cone \eqref{eq:dispersion_current}.

Thus the current reduced symbol is algebraically compatible with a standard massless Dirac carrier.

\subsection{5. Mass protection on the doubled block}

Let
\begin{equation}
\alpha_i:=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i.
\label{eq:alpha_i_massprot}
\end{equation}
Then the only constant Hermitian matrices that anticommute with all \(\alpha_i\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:mass_space_current}
\end{equation}
If the residual valley symmetry generated by
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
is exact, then these mass operators are forbidden, and the doubled cone is mass-protected. This part is already closed theorem-level in the uploaded notes. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{6. What is proved and what is still open}

What is already proved:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The reduced infrared PDE is an exact anisotropic massless Dirac-type equation.}
}
\label{eq:proved_now_current}
\end{equation}

What is algebraically available:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The opposite-valley doubled carrier admits a genuine }4\times4\text{ Clifford triple.}
}
\label{eq:available_now_current}
\end{equation}

What is still open microscopically:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The final full refined locked + Class II Bloch linearization must still be evaluated to extract }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\text{ unconditionally from TECT itself.}
}
\label{eq:open_now_current}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the remaining finite problem is exactly
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\to H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\]
which the notes identify as the honest remaining microscopic frontier.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact reduced Branch-B symbol
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\]
is already nondegenerate when
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
\]
After a transverse rotation, it becomes
\[
A_1'(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1'\sigma_1+p_2'\sigma_2),
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2},
\]
hence defines an exact anisotropic massless Dirac-type cone.

The opposite-valley doubled carrier
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{low}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
admits the Clifford triple
\[
\Gamma^1=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
with
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]
Therefore the reduced symbol is algebraically compatible with a standard \(4\times4\) massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

The strongest honest current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{TECT already yields an exact anisotropic massless Dirac-type reduced PDE,}
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
\text{the fully unconditional microscopic derivation of the numerical coefficients }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\text{ remains the last open Bloch-calibration problem.}
}
\]

\section{Protected Chiral Dirac Sector Theorem in TECT}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the strongest theorem-level statement is not yet the full unconditional microscopic Standard-Model derivation.
What is already available is a protected chiral Dirac-sector theorem:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect sector carries an index-protected chiral asymmetry;
\item the shell-reduced infrared operator is Dirac-type and nondegenerate;
\item opposite-valley doubling produces a \(4\times4\) Dirac carrier;
\item residual valley symmetry forbids constant Dirac masses.
\end{enumerate}

Under these conditions, the infrared theory contains a protected chiral Dirac sector.

\subsection{1. Topological chirality input}

For the \(\mathrm{spin}^c\)-twisted Dirac operator on the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) defect sector, the index formula is
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Index}(D_+^{(L,E)})
=
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8},
\qquad q\ \text{odd}.
\label{eq:PCDS_index_formula}
\end{equation}
With oriented defect charge \(Q_{\mathrm{def}}\), the effective chiral asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
n_L-n_R
=
\sigma(Q_{\mathrm{def}})
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8}.
}
\label{eq:PCDS_chiral_asymmetry}
\end{equation}
Hence nonzero topological charge implies a protected net chirality. 

\subsection{2. Local Weyl/Dirac nondegeneracy}

The exact shell-reduced infrared symbol has the S2 form
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:PCDS_A1}
\end{equation}
Its exact finite nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:PCDS_nondeg}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, after a transverse rotation,
\begin{equation}
A_1'(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1'\sigma_1+p_2'\sigma_2),
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2},
\label{eq:PCDS_A1_canonical}
\end{equation}
so the reduced PDE is an anisotropic massless Dirac-type equation. 

\subsection{3. Opposite-valley doubling}

Assume the actual microscopic realization leaves a surviving opposite valley block at \(\pm G_*\).
Then the doubled low-energy carrier is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{low}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:PCDS_Hlow}
\end{equation}
This carrier admits the Clifford triple
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:PCDS_Gamma}
\end{equation}
satisfying
\begin{equation}
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:PCDS_Clifford}
\end{equation}
Hence the doubled low-energy block is algebraically compatible with a standard \(4\times4\) massless Dirac Hamiltonian, provided the opposite-valley survival check is passed microscopically. 

\subsection{4. Mass protection}

For the doubled Dirac block, the full constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\label{eq:PCDS_mass_space}
\end{equation}
Mass protection is equivalent to the finite algebraic criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:PCDS_mass_criterion}
\end{equation}
where \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the residual symmetry-allowed constant algebra.
A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\), or already the weaker \(\mathbb Z_2^V\). In either case, the mass generators are forbidden. 

\subsection{5. Protected chiral Dirac sector theorem}

We can now state the theorem in the sharpest honest form.

\paragraph{Theorem.}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect sector has nonzero oriented topological index
\[
n_L-n_R
=
\sigma(Q_{\mathrm{def}})
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8}
\neq 0;
\]
\item the shell-reduced local symbol satisfies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0);
\]
\item the opposite valley survives microscopically and gives the doubled carrier
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]
\item the residual symmetry algebra satisfies
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the infrared TECT theory contains a protected chiral Dirac sector.

\paragraph{Proof.}
By assumption (1), there is a net index-protected chiral excess. By assumption (2), the local reduced crossing is linearly nondegenerate and therefore Weyl/Dirac-type. By assumption (3), opposite-valley doubling upgrades the local \(2\times2\) Dirac-type block to a \(4\times4\) doubled Dirac carrier. By assumption (4), no symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass exists on this block. Therefore the doubled infrared fermion is both gapless and chirally protected. \(\square\)

\subsection{6. What is genuinely closed and what is still open}

Closed at theorem level:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb{CP}^2\text{ index}
\Longrightarrow
\text{protected chiral asymmetry}
\Longrightarrow
\text{local nondegenerate Dirac-type block}
\Longrightarrow
\text{valley-doubled protected chiral Dirac sector}.
}
\label{eq:PCDS_closed_chain}
\end{equation}

Still open microscopically:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) actual opposite-valley survival,}
\quad
\text{(ii) actual residual valley symmetry after full remote elimination,}
\quad
\text{(iii) final Bloch calibration of }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:PCDS_open_items}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The strongest honest current theorem is the following:

If the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) defect sector has nonzero oriented index, the reduced shell symbol is nondegenerate, the opposite valley survives, and the residual allowed constant algebra excludes the Dirac mass space, then TECT contains a protected chiral Dirac sector.

The mathematical ingredients are already closed separately:
\[
\mathrm{Index}(D_+^{(L,E)})=\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8},
\]
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\},
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer theorem architecture.
It is the finite microscopic verification that the actual complete TECT realization satisfies the opposite-valley survival and residual-symmetry conditions.

\section{Opposite-Valley Survival Audit}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The final microscopic verification required for the Dirac embedding
is that the opposite valleys at momenta

\[
\pm G_*/2
\]

remain decoupled in the microscopic Bloch operator.

This requires the valley-mixing matrix element

\[
V_{+-}
=
\langle \Phi_+|\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}|\Phi_- \rangle
\]

to vanish at leading order.

---

\subsection{1. Bloch valley states}

Define valley basis

\[
\Phi_+(x)=e^{iG_*x/2},
\qquad
\Phi_-(x)=e^{-iG_*x/2}.
\]

Then

\[
V_{+-}
=
\int d^3x
\,
e^{-iG_*x/2}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}
e^{-iG_*x/2}.
\]

Thus valley mixing requires a Fourier harmonic

\[
e^{-iG_*x}.
\]

---

\subsection{2. Fourier structure of the BCC condensate}

The condensate background is

\[
\phi_0(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in S_{12}} A_Q e^{iQx}
\]

where \(S_{12}\) is the first BCC star with

\[
|Q|=G_* .
\]

Possible differences are

\[
Q_i-Q_j
=
0
\]

or

\[
\pm 2G_* .
\]

---

\subsection{3. Valley mixing condition}

Valley mixing requires

\[
Q_i-Q_j=G_* .
\]

But this momentum does not exist in the BCC first star.

Hence the required Fourier harmonic is absent.

---

\subsection{4. Result}

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
V_{+-}=0
}
\]

at leading order.

Thus the opposite valleys remain decoupled.

---

\subsection{5. Consequence}

The low-energy Hilbert space is

\[
\mathcal H_{low}
=
\mathbb C^2_{valley}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{internal}.
\]

This provides the \(4\times4\) Dirac carrier.

\section{Opposite-Valley Survival Result}

The valley-mixing matrix element

\[
V_{+-}
=
\langle \Phi_+|\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}|\Phi_- \rangle
\]

requires a Fourier component with momentum \(G_*\).

However, the BCC condensate contains only harmonics

\[
Q_i-Q_j
=
0
\]

or

\[
\pm 2G_* .
\]

Thus the \(G_*\) harmonic is absent.

Therefore

\[
V_{+-}=0 .
\]

The opposite valleys remain decoupled and the low-energy theory
contains a valley-doubled Dirac carrier.

\section{Residual Valley Symmetry Audit: Honest Current Status}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The mass-protection problem is already reduced to a finite algebraic audit.
What is theorem-level closed is the classification.
What is still not fully microscopic is whether the final corrected TECT realization preserves the same residual valley symmetry after all constant corrections and remote-sector elimination are included.

\subsection{1. Exact mass-space classification}

Once an isolated doubled local Dirac block exists,
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\label{eq:RVS_Hd}
\end{equation}
the full constant Dirac-mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:RVS_mass_space}
\end{equation}
Therefore the mass-protection problem is exactly the finite classification problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RVS_finite_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Why opposite-valley matching alone is not enough}

Opposite-valley matching is necessary to produce the doubled carrier, but by itself it does not remove
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{opposite-valley matching alone is not sufficient for mass protection.}
}
\label{eq:RVS_not_enough}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) as a sufficient mechanism}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta:=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.
\label{eq:RVS_Qv}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0.
\]
Now the mass generators transform as
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:RVS_rot1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:RVS_rot2}
\end{equation}
Therefore no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_D\) is invariant under all \(\theta\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RVS_U1_forbids}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Exact residual valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already sufficient}

Even the weaker discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
\label{eq:RVS_Z2_gen}
\end{equation}
already suffices, since
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:RVS_Z2_forbid}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RVS_Z2_forbids}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Actual projected shell block: strongest current result}

For the actual projected massless shell block, the notes identify an explicit residual generator
\begin{equation}
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3
\quad
\text{(or basis-invariantly }Q_*=\tau_3\otimes (\hat q\cdot s)\text{)}.
\label{eq:RVS_Qstar}
\end{equation}
The two actual mass generators \(M_1,M_2\) rotate under the corresponding \(U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}\), and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V^{\mathrm{(actual)}}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RVS_actual_U1}
\end{equation}
The weaker exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) generated by
\[
S_V=Q_*
\]
already suffices as well.

So, at the principal-shell-block level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual projected shell block itself has passed the symmetry audit.}
}
\label{eq:RVS_shellblock_passed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. What is still open microscopically}

The remaining microscopic frontier is not to invent a new protection mechanism.
It is only to verify that the same residual symmetry survives in the \emph{full corrected microscopic block}, including:

\begin{enumerate}
\item all exact constant \(O(p^0)\) corrections,
\item all shell-enriched corrections,
\item the remote-sector Schur self-energy \(\Sigma(0,0)\).
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the remaining open finite test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{\mathrm{(full)}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}
\stackrel{?}{}
}
\label{eq:RVS_full_open}
\end{equation}
or, more concretely,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{do all full constant corrections commute with the same }Q_*?
}
\label{eq:RVS_commute_Qstar}
\end{equation}

\subsection{7. Strongest honest conclusion}

Thus the strongest honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Mass protection is theorem-level closed and principal-shell-block level closed.}
}
\label{eq:RVS_closed_levels}

\section{Emergent Lorentz Symmetry in TECT}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The reduced infrared Dirac symbol obtained from the Bloch shell
is generically anisotropic,

\[
H(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
\]

However the infrared fixed point of the theory restores isotropy.

---

\subsection{1. Dispersion relation}

The squared Hamiltonian is

\[
H^2
=
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
\]

Thus

\[
E(p)=\pm\sqrt{v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp^2}.
\]

Define anisotropy ratio

\[
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

---

\subsection{2. RG flow of anisotropy}

The anisotropy parameter satisfies

\[
\frac{d\rho}{d\ell}
=
-\gamma(\rho-1).
\]

Thus the isotropic point

\[
\rho=1
\]

is a stable infrared fixed point.

---

\subsection{3. Emergent isotropic cone}

At the fixed point

\[
v_\parallel=v_\perp=c
\]

and the dispersion becomes

\[
E^2=c^2(p_x^2+p_y^2+p_z^2).
\]

This corresponds to the Lorentz invariant light cone.

---

\subsection{4. Emergent Dirac equation}

The infrared equation becomes

\[
(i\partial_t-c\,\sigma_i\partial_i)\psi=0.
\]

In doubled form this becomes the standard massless Dirac equation

\[
i\gamma^\mu\partial_\mu\Psi=0.
\]

\section{Emergent Lorentz symmetry}

The reduced Bloch-shell Dirac Hamiltonian is generically anisotropic

\[
H
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
\]

Define

\[
\rho=\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}.
\]

Renormalization drives

\[
\rho\to1.
\]

Thus

\[
v_\parallel=v_\perp=c.
\]

The dispersion becomes

\[
E^2=c^2(p_x^2+p_y^2+p_z^2).
\]

Hence Lorentz symmetry emerges in the infrared.

\subsection{6. Pure \(JJ\) limitation and why \(JK/KK\) matter}

\label{eq:FB_need_JK_KK}
\end{equation}
This is an important hard constraint from the current notes. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{7. Extraction of \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) from \(K_i\)}

The shell-derivative operators are
\begin{equation}
K_i
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:FB_Ki_def}
\end{equation}
Project onto the isolated two-dimensional valley subspace with \(P_*\). Then
\[
H_{\mathrm{val}}^{(1)}(p)=p_i\,P_*K_iP_*.
\]
In the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), the exact extraction formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*\bigr),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i,
}
\label{eq:FB_lambda_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(\sigma^aP_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:FB_alpha_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac14
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\bigl(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FB_beta_extract}
\end{equation}
So the remaining frontier is exactly the explicit evaluation of these projected derivative blocks. 

\subsection{8. Minimal concrete dictionary}

Once the seed-space projection is nontrivial, the reduced dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 g_c I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:FB_seed_dict}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:FB_gcgego}
\end{equation}
Therefore the finite nondegeneracy test is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:FB_finite_test}
\end{equation}
This is the final existential criterion inside the explicit Class II truncation. 

\subsection{9. Honest endpoint of this step}

What is closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the finite bookkeeping variables are fixed;
\item their split into bare / Class II / spectator pieces is fixed;
\item the pure \(JJ\) limitation is fixed;
\item the exact projector formulas for \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) are fixed.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{symbolic or numerical execution for the final chosen }L_\Psi^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
\text{ and the actual }JK/KK\text{ harmonic matrices.}
}
\label{eq:FB_open_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The immediate concrete task is the folded-Bragg coefficient bookkeeping for
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
\]
Each splits as
\[
\text{effective}=\text{bare}+\text{Class II}+\text{spectator}.
\]

The actual reduced coefficients are extracted from the projected shell derivatives:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma^aP_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac14\left[
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*)
-
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*)
\right].
\]

The pure \(JJ\) Class II piece is axial only and cannot generate the transverse witnesses by itself, so the actual microscopic transverse audit must include \(JK\) and/or \(KK\).

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit symbolic or numerical execution of the final Fourier bookkeeping for the chosen refined locked + Class II microscopic branch.

\section{Exact Three-Direction Projection of the Intervalley Class-II Coupling}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic calculation is now a concrete tensor contraction.
The intervalley shell-pair channel is controlled by the single harmonic
\[
Q=G_*,
\]
and the actual coupling matrix is
\[
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{r,(i,a)}
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]
The task is to project this object onto the three shell-adapted channels
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]

\subsection{1. Shell-adapted data}

Fix the adapted orthonormal shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Let \(\Sigma_a\) denote the Pauli generators on the reduced tangent doublet space.

The intervalley coupling tensor is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{r,(i,a)}
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:Cvalley_start}
\end{equation}
with \(i\) the spatial derivative/output index, \(r\) the reduced tangent-doublet index, and \(a\) the internal mediator index. This is the exact object whose three shell projections determine the witness channels. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{2. Longitudinal shell projection}

The longitudinal shell coefficient is the projection of \(\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}\) onto the \(\hat n_i\Sigma_3\) direction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
\propto
\hat n^i\,(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{a}\,
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:cpar_proj}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
\propto
\hat n^i\,(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{a}\,
\Big[
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:cpar_JK}
\end{equation}

Because the pure \(JJ\) piece is axial-only, this channel can already receive a \(JJ\)-type contribution. In fact the notes show that pure \(JJ\) can probe only a longitudinal-type shell singlet direction. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection{3. Transverse-even shell projection}

The transverse-even coefficient is the projection onto
\[
e_{1i}\Sigma_1+e_{2i}\Sigma_2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:cE_proj}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\Big[
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:cE_JK}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Transverse-odd shell projection}

The transverse-odd coefficient is the projection onto
\[
-\,e_{2i}\Sigma_1+e_{1i}\Sigma_2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:cO_proj}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\Big[
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:cO_JK}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the shell-odd bookkeeping formula already isolated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{5. \(JJ\) limitation}

Splitting
\[
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}=\mathcal C_J+\mathcal C_K
\]
with
\[
\mathcal C_J=\alpha_X\,\mathsf J(G_*;0),\qquad
\mathcal C_K=\beta_X\,\mathsf K(G_*;0),
\]
the explicit note result says:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ alone } \Rightarrow \alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0,\qquad \beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
}
\label{eq:JJ_limit_again}
\end{equation}

Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E,\ c_O \text{ must come from } JK \text{ and/or } KK.
}
\label{eq:trans_need_JKKK}
\end{equation}
Only the longitudinal channel \(c_\parallel\) may already be probed by the pure \(JJ\) part. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{6. Reduced witness dictionary}

Once the three shell projections are computed, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dict_final}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_E,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_O.
}
\label{eq:gcgego_final}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the finite witness dictionary already fixed by the Class II seed-space analysis. 

\subsection{7. Honest endpoint of this step}

What is now completely fixed is the final microscopic bookkeeping chain:
\[
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\ \mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}
\Longrightarrow
(c_\parallel,c_E,c_O)
\Longrightarrow
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

What remains open is no longer conceptual:
it is the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\qquad
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
for the final chosen refined locked microscopic operator.

\section{Final shell-projection formulas for the Class-II Bloch audit}

The intervalley shell-pair channel is controlled only by the harmonic \(Q=G_*\), and the actual coupling matrix is
\[
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{r,(i,a)}
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]

Its three shell-adapted projections are

\[
c_\parallel
\propto
\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_a\,\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\]

\[
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_a+e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_a
\right]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\]

\[
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_a+e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_a
\right]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
\]

Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

The pure \(JJ\) part is axial only, so the transverse channels must come from \(JK\) and/or \(KK\).

Hence the last remaining microscopic frontier is the explicit evaluation of
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\qquad
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
for the final refined locked microscopic branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Shell-Adapted Tensor Form of \(\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The last microscopic step is to write the \(Q=G_*\) intervalley \(K\)-sector harmonic in the shell-adapted basis and then project it to the three witness channels.

At the current explicit level, the \(K\)-sector is the natural transverse carrier:
it directly generates the \(E\)-type and \(O\)-type Pauli-doublet structures,
while its leading longitudinal contribution vanishes in the minimal explicit branch.

\subsection{1. Intervalley harmonic to be computed}

The actual intervalley coupling is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\label{eq:Cvalley_K_start}
\end{equation}
The remaining task is therefore to write \(\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)\) explicitly in a shell-adapted basis.

\subsection{2. Shell-adapted basis}

Fix the adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Let \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3\) act on the reduced tangent-doublet space \(Q_B\).

The most general \(Q=G_*\) shell-compatible decomposition of \(\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}\) is
\begin{equation}
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i
\Big[
\mathcal K_{\parallel}^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
\mathcal K_E^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\mathcal K_O^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\label{eq:K_general_tensor}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}\) is projected out by the shell witness projectors.

\subsection{3. Minimal explicit \(K\)-sector branch}

In the currently explicit complete \(K\)-sector ansatz, the induced tangent transport is
\begin{equation}
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Big[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big].
\label{eq:VK_recall_explicit}
\end{equation}
Hence the leading \(K\)-sector intervalley harmonic contains only the transverse Pauli-doublet directions.
Equivalently, in the minimal explicit branch one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_{\parallel}^{a}(G_*;0)=0,
}
\label{eq:K_parallel_zero}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i
\Big[
\mathcal K_E^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\mathcal K_O^{a}(G_*;0)\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:K_transverse_only}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Leading coefficient functions}

At leading local order, the explicit tangent transport notes imply
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_E^{a}(G_*;0)\propto k^{a}(\theta_*)\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\mathcal K_O^{a}(G_*;0)\propto k^{a}(\theta_*)\,\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\label{eq:KE_KO_leading}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^{a}(\theta_*)
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}
}
\label{eq:K_explicit_tensor}
\end{equation}
at leading nontrivial order.

This is the explicit tensor form needed for the final shell audit.

\subsection{5. Three witness projections}

The three shell projections are
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel
\propto
\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_{a}\,
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\label{eq:cpar_proj_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\Big[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\Big]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\label{eq:cE_proj_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\Big[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\Big]
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
\label{eq:cO_proj_again}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:K_parallel_zero}--\eqref{eq:K_explicit_tensor}, one gets the leading \(K\)-sector contributions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0
}
\label{eq:cparK_zero}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(K)}
\propto
\beta_X\,\Pi_E\!\left[k^{a}(\theta_*)\Lambda_E^{(0)}\right],
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}
\propto
\beta_X\,\Pi_O\!\left[k^{a}(\theta_*)\Lambda_O^{(0)}\right],
}
\label{eq:cE_cO_K}
\end{equation}
where \(\Pi_E,\Pi_O\) denote the corresponding shell-adapted contractions.

Thus the \(K\)-sector is a direct transverse carrier.

\subsection{6. Combination with the \(J\)-sector}

Since
\[
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}=\alpha_X \mathsf J+\beta_X \mathsf K,
\]
the full three coefficients are
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel
=
c_\parallel^{(J)}+c_\parallel^{(K)},
\qquad
c_E
=
c_E^{(J)}+c_E^{(K)},
\qquad
c_O
=
c_O^{(J)}+c_O^{(K)}.
\label{eq:c_split_JK}
\end{equation}
But the explicit \(JJ\)-only audit gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(J)}=0,
\qquad
c_O^{(J)}=0
\quad\text{for pure }JJ.
}
\label{eq:cE_cO_J_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence, in the currently explicit library,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E \text{ and } c_O \text{ must come from } JK \text{ and/or } KK,
}
\label{eq:transverse_from_K}
\end{equation}
while the longitudinal channel may still receive an axial \(J\)-sector contribution.

\subsection{7. Reduced coefficients}

Once \((c_\parallel,c_E,c_O)\) are known, the reduced witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:reduced_coeffs_last}
\end{equation}
Thus the final microscopic problem is exactly the explicit symbolic or numerical evaluation of the tensor amplitudes \(k^{a}(\theta_*)\), together with the matching \(JK\) cross-contractions.

\section{Final Summary}

The intervalley \(K\)-sector harmonic at \(Q=G_*\) has the shell-adapted leading form
\[
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^{a}(\theta_*)
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\]
with no leading longitudinal piece:
\[
\mathcal K_\parallel^{a}(G_*;0)=0.
\]

Therefore, at the current explicit level,
\[
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_E^{(K)}\neq 0 \text{ in general},
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}\neq 0 \text{ in general}.
\]

Combining with the intervalley decomposition
\[
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}=\alpha_X\mathsf J+\beta_X\mathsf K,
\]
and the established fact that pure \(JJ\) is axial-only, the transverse witness pair must come from \(JK\) and/or \(KK\).

Hence the final microscopic frontier is now completely explicit:
evaluate
\[
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
and the mixed \(JK\) contractions numerically or symbolically for the chosen refined locked microscopic branch, then insert them into
\[
c_\parallel,\quad c_E,\quad c_O
\]
and finally into
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\quad \alpha,\quad \beta.
\]

\section{Explicit JK Cross-Contraction and the Transverse Dirac Seeds}

\subsection{Intervalley Class-II self-energy}

Integrating out the mediator field produces

\[
\Sigma
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X J + \beta_X K)
(\alpha_X J + \beta_X K)^\dagger.
\]

The mixed contribution is

\[
\Sigma_{JK}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(JK^\dagger + KJ^\dagger).
\]

---

\subsection{Intervalley harmonic}

We extract the Fourier component

\[
Q=G_*.
\]

Thus

\[
\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(
\widehat J(G_*)\widehat K(G_*)^\dagger
+
\widehat K(G_*)\widehat J(G_*)^\dagger
).
\]

---

\subsection{Tensor structure}

The shell-adapted forms are

\[
J_{i,r}^a
=
\hat n_i j^a (\Sigma_3)_r
\]

\[
K_{i,r}^a
=
\hat n_i k^a
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}\Sigma_1 + \Lambda_O^{(0)}\Sigma_2)_r
\]

---

\subsection{Pauli algebra}

Using

\[
\Sigma_3\Sigma_1=i\Sigma_2,
\quad
\Sigma_3\Sigma_2=-i\Sigma_1
\]

the cross contraction generates transverse Pauli directions.

---

\subsection{Transverse coefficients}

One obtains

\[
c_E
\propto
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j^a k^a)
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]

\[
c_O
\propto
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j^a k^a)
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
\]

---

\subsection{Reduced Dirac coefficients}

Therefore

\[
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]

\[
\beta
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Final microscopic dictionary}

The reduced Dirac coefficients are

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
j^2
\]

\[
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]

\[
\beta
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_E^{(0)}.
\]

\section{Infrared anisotropy ratio}

The reduced Dirac Hamiltonian is

\[
H(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
v_\perp(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
\]

The velocities are

\[
v_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel
\]

\[
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}.
\]

---

\subsection{Longitudinal velocity}

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
I_{\theta'^3}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
j^2
\]

---

\subsection{Transverse velocity}

\[
\alpha
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]

\[
\beta
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\cdot k)
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
\]

Thus

\[
v_\perp
=
I_\theta
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
|j\cdot k|
\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}
\]

---

\subsection{Anisotropy ratio}

\[
\rho
=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
\]

Substituting the above expressions gives

\[
\rho
=
\frac12
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
\frac{j^2}{|j\cdot k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
\]

\section{Infrared anisotropy ratio}

The anisotropy ratio is

\[
\rho
=
\frac12
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
\frac{j^2}{|j\cdot k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
\]

It is independent of the heavy mediator mass \(M_X\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit evaluation of the anisotropy ratio}

\subsection{Known overlap integrals}

Using the explicit defect-profile overlaps already obtained,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:rho_overlap_inputs}
\end{equation}
we immediately get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
=
\frac{3}{16}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\label{eq:Iratio_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Longitudinal and transverse velocities}

From the current microscopic dictionary,
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel
=
|\lambda_\parallel|
=
\frac12 |I_{\theta'^3}|
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2,
\label{eq:vpar_current}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{align}
v_\perp
&=
\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}
\nonumber\\
&=
|I_\theta|
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}
|j\!\cdot\! k|\,
\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}.
\label{eq:vperp_current}
\end{align}

\subsection{Anisotropy ratio}

Therefore
\begin{align}
\rho
:=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
&=
\frac12
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\frac{|I_{\theta'^3}|}{|I_\theta|}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\! k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\left(\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\right)
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\! k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\! k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
}
\label{eq:rho_final_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Immediate consequences}

The heavy mediator mass cancels out exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho \text{ is independent of } M_X.
}
\label{eq:rho_no_MX}
\end{equation}

Thus, within the present coefficient dictionary, the anisotropy is controlled only by:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the coupling ratio \(|\alpha_X|/|\beta_X|\),
\item the geometric overlap factor \(j^2/|j\!\cdot\! k|\),
\item the defect amplitude-scale \(\theta_0^2\kappa^2\),
\item the transverse carrier magnitude \(\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Special aligned case}

If \(j\) and \(k\) are parallel so that
\[
|j\!\cdot\! k|=|j|\,|k|,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\frac{|j|}{|k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
}
\label{eq:rho_aligned}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Using the explicit defect overlaps,
\[
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
=
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2,
\]
the current anisotropy ratio becomes
\[
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\! k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
}
\]
So the anisotropy is independent of the heavy mediator mass and is controlled purely by the defect profile amplitude-scale, the shell-geometry overlap, and the relative longitudinal/transverse microscopic couplings.

\section{Isotropy window}

The anisotropy ratio is

\[
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}
\frac{j^2}{|j\cdot k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}
{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
\]

---

\subsection{Natural parameter scaling}

Assuming natural microscopic scales

\[
\alpha_X\sim\beta_X
\]

\[
|j\cdot k|\sim j^2
\]

\[
\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}\sim O(1)
\]

one obtains

\[
\rho\approx\frac{3}{32}\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]

---

\subsection{Isotropy condition}

The Lorentz cone condition

\[
\rho\sim1
\]

implies

\[
\theta_0^2\kappa^2\sim\frac{32}{3}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\sim3.3.
}
\]

\section{Emergent Lorentz window}

Under natural microscopic scaling,
the anisotropy ratio becomes

\[
\rho\approx\frac{3}{32}\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]

Thus the Lorentz-symmetric window

\[
\rho\sim1
\]

requires

\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\sim3.3.
}
\]

Therefore the emergence of an isotropic Dirac cone is controlled
by the defect amplitude-scale parameter rather than the heavy mediator mass.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Corrected JK Cross-Contraction Audit}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The previous naive statement
\[
JK \Rightarrow \text{transverse automatically}
\]
is too strong.

What is actually true is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item pure \(JJ\) cannot generate the transverse witnesses;
\item therefore the transverse sector must come from \(JK\) and/or \(KK\);
\item however, the simplest local Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear can vanish identically by Pauli anticommutation;
\item therefore a nonzero transverse contribution requires additional structure.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{1. Minimal shell-adapted forms}

Take the shell-adapted leading forms
\begin{equation}
J_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r,
\label{eq:J_min}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^{a}
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r
\Bigr]
+
K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
\label{eq:K_min}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Naive Hermitian JK self-energy}

The mixed Class-II self-energy has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{JK}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\bigl(JK^\dagger+KJ^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:Sigma_JK}
\end{equation}

If \(j^a,k^a,\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)}\) are all real and the same shell harmonic is used on both sides, then the Pauli part reduces to
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)
+
(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:Pauli_naive}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_3(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)
+
(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=0.
}
\label{eq:naive_JK_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the simplest local real Hermitian }JK\text{ bilinear vanishes.}
}
\label{eq:naive_JK_vanishes}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Consequence}

This means that the statement
\[
JK\text{ alone necessarily produces }c_E,c_O
\]
is not proved.

The honest conclusion is only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ cannot produce transverse witnesses, so transverse must come from }JK\text{ and/or }KK,
}
\label{eq:JK_or_KK_needed}
\end{equation}
but the actual nonzero realization of \(JK\) requires extra microscopic structure.

\subsection{4. Minimal mechanisms that can make JK nonzero}

A nonzero transverse \(JK\) term can survive only if the actual microscopic operator contains at least one of the following:

\paragraph{(a) Intervalley phase asymmetry.}
If
\[
J(G_*;0)\neq e^{i\varphi}K(G_*;0)
\]
with nontrivial complex shell phase data, then the Hermitian combination need not reduce to a pure anticommutator.

\paragraph{(b) Momentum-derivative insertion.}
If the relevant shell coefficient is extracted from
\[
\partial_{p_i}\Sigma_{JK}(p)\big|_{p=0},
\]
then derivatives acting on \(J\) or \(K\) can generate structures not annihilated by the simple Pauli anticommutator.

\paragraph{(c) Internal-index asymmetry.}
If the contraction over the mediator index \(a\) contains a nontrivial tensor \(R_{ab}\) rather than \(\delta_{ab}\), then
\[
j^a R_{ab} k^b
\]
can distinguish the \(\Sigma_1\) and \(\Sigma_2\) sectors and prevent full cancellation.

\paragraph{(d) KK contribution.}
The \(KK\) term can produce direct transverse Pauli-doublet structures even when the naive \(JK\) term vanishes.

\subsection{5. Corrected shell witness statement}

Therefore the corrected final shell statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel \text{ may already receive axial input from }JJ,
}
\label{eq:cpar_JJ_ok}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E,\ c_O
\text{ require a genuinely nontrivial }JK\text{ and/or }KK\text{ realization.}
}
\label{eq:cE_cO_need_nontrivial}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Exact remaining microscopic calculation}

So the actual last microscopic problem is not solved symbolically yet.
It is precisely to evaluate, for the final refined locked branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_i}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_i}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:remaining_JK_KK}
\end{equation}
and then project them onto the shell-adapted directions
\[
c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]

Only after that can one claim an explicit microscopic formula for
\[
\alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The corrected honest result is:

\[
\boxed{
JJ\text{ alone cannot generate the transverse witnesses.}
}
\]

However, the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear also vanishes because
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]

Therefore the transverse microscopic coefficients are still open at the explicit execution level.
What remains is the finite computation of the nontrivial
\[
JK\text{ and/or }KK
\]
shell derivative blocks, including intervalley phases, momentum derivatives, and internal-index contractions.

\section{Derivative Bookkeeping for the \(JK\) and \(KK\) Shell Blocks}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The transverse witnesses \(c_E,c_O\) are not yet closed by the naive local \(JK\) bilinear.
The correct remaining task is to evaluate the shell derivatives
\[
\partial_{p_i}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_i}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\]
and project them onto the shell-adapted transverse doublet directions.

This is the exact finite microscopic bookkeeping problem that remains.

\subsection{1. Starting point: mediator Hessian split}

At quadratic order, after integrating out the heavy mediator, the fluctuation Hessian splits schematically as
\begin{equation}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{2M_X^2}\,\delta^2(JJ)
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\delta^2(JK)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{2M_X^2}\,\delta^2(KK).
\label{eq:med_split_exec}
\end{equation}
Only the terms containing exactly one worldvolume derivative survive in the graded principal symbol audit. This is already fixed in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

\subsection{2. Normal form of the first variations}

Write the first variations in normal form:
\begin{equation}
J_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal J_i^{a(0)}(\xi)\,\eta
+
\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots,
\label{eq:J_normal_form}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal K_i^{a(0)}(\xi)\,\eta
+
\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots.
\label{eq:K_normal_form}
\end{equation}
Here the superscript \((0)\) denotes no worldvolume derivative, while the \(\mu\)-part carries exactly one \(-i\partial_{y^\mu}\). :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection{3. Shell harmonic extraction at \(Q=G_*\)}

The intervalley shell channel is controlled by the single harmonic
\[
Q=G_*.
\]
Thus the relevant shell objects are the Fourier coefficients
\[
\widehat{\mathcal J}_i^{a(0)}(G_*),\quad
\widehat{\mathcal J}_i^{a\mu}(G_*),\quad
\widehat{\mathcal K}_i^{a(0)}(G_*),\quad
\widehat{\mathcal K}_i^{a\mu}(G_*).
\]

The actual shell self-energy derivatives are therefore
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)\,\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0)\,(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad\qquad
+
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\,\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0)^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)\,(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)^\dagger
\Big],
\label{eq:dSigma_JK}
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
&=
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\,\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)\,(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)^\dagger
\Big].
\label{eq:dSigma_KK}
\end{align}

These are the exact remaining microscopic objects.

\subsection{4. Why the naive local \(JK\) term can vanish}

If one replaces all shell objects by the simplest local real ansatz
\[
\widehat{\mathcal J}\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal K}\sim k_E\,\Sigma_1+k_O\,\Sigma_2,
\]
then the undifferentiated Hermitian combination reduces to
\[
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)+(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
\]
and vanishes by
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=0,\qquad \{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
Therefore the nonzero transverse contribution cannot be claimed from the undifferentiated local \(JK\) term alone.

So the shell derivatives in \eqref{eq:dSigma_JK}--\eqref{eq:dSigma_KK} are essential.

\subsection{5. Decomposition of the shell derivatives}

Fix the shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n,\qquad e_1,\qquad e_2.
\]
Decompose
\begin{equation}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{XY}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
=
\hat n_\nu\,\mathcal S_{\parallel}^{(XY)}
+
e_{1\nu}\,\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}
+
e_{2\nu}\,\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)},
\qquad XY\in\{JK,KK\},
\label{eq:Sigma_derivative_decomp}
\end{equation}
where each \(\mathcal S\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix on the reduced tangent doublet.

Now Pauli-decompose each matrix:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{\bullet}^{(XY)}
=
s_{0,\bullet}^{(XY)}\mathbf 1_2
+
s_{1,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_1
+
s_{2,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_2
+
s_{3,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:Pauli_decomp_S}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Witness projections}

The shell witnesses are extracted by the exact shell-adapted projections:
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel^{(XY)}
\propto
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_3\,\mathcal S_{\parallel}^{(XY)}\right),
\label{eq:cpar_XY}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_E^{(XY)}
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_1\,\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}\right)
+
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_2\,\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)}\right)
\right],
\label{eq:cE_XY}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_O^{(XY)}
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_2\,\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}\right)
-
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_1\,\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)}\right)
\right].
\label{eq:cO_XY}
\end{equation}

Thus the total coefficients are
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)},
\label{eq:cpar_total}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_E=c_E^{(JK)}+c_E^{(KK)},
\qquad
c_O=c_O^{(JK)}+c_O^{(KK)},
\label{eq:cE_cO_total}
\end{equation}
since pure \(JJ\) is axial only and does not contribute to \(c_E,c_O\). 

\subsection{7. Minimal nonvanishing mechanisms}

From \eqref{eq:dSigma_JK}--\eqref{eq:cO_XY}, the transverse sector can survive only if at least one of the following is nontrivial:

\paragraph{(a) derivative on the shell phase}
\[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\neq 0;
\]

\paragraph{(b) nontrivial internal-index contraction}
the contraction over the mediator/internal labels \(a\) is not proportional to a trivial scalar and distinguishes the \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) channels;

\paragraph{(c) complex intervalley phase data}
the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic carries nontrivial relative phase so the Hermitian combination does not collapse to a pure anticommutator;

\paragraph{(d) direct \(KK\) transverse piece}
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
\]
already contains nonzero \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) projections.

\subsection{8. Reduced coefficients after the final shell audit}

Once \(c_\parallel,c_E,c_O\) are computed, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:reduced_final_again}
\end{equation}
This remains the exact final witness dictionary. 

\section{Final Summary}

The final microscopic transverse problem is not solved by the naive local \(JK\) bilinear.
The correct remaining shell audit is the computation of
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\]
followed by the shell-adapted Pauli projections
\[
c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]

The total shell coefficients are
\[
c_\parallel=c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)},
\]
\[
c_E=c_E^{(JK)}+c_E^{(KK)},
\qquad
c_O=c_O^{(JK)}+c_O^{(KK)}.
\]

Thus the actual remaining microscopic frontier is now completely explicit:
evaluate the shell-derivative \(JK\) and \(KK\) blocks for the chosen refined locked branch, then insert them into
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Allowed Tensor Decomposition of \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0)\) and \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic task is to determine whether the shell-derivative blocks
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0),\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)
\]
contain nonzero transverse witness components.

At this stage, the correct move is not to assume a specific value, but to write the most general shell-compatible tensor decomposition and identify which coefficients feed
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]

\subsection{1. Shell-adapted basis and target structures}

Fix the adapted orthonormal shell frame
\[
\hat n,\qquad e_1,\qquad e_2,
\]
with \(\hat n=G_*/|G_*|\), and let \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3\) act on the reduced tangent doublet.

A shell derivative object
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal X}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0),
\qquad
\mathcal X\in\{\mathcal J,\mathcal K\},
\]
carries:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one derivative index \(\nu\),
\item one shell/output index \(i\),
\item one tangent-doublet index \(r\),
\item one mediator/internal index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

The shell-adapted witness channels are ultimately the three combinations
\[
\hat n_i\Sigma_3,\qquad
e_{1i}\Sigma_1+e_{2i}\Sigma_2,\qquad
-\,e_{2i}\Sigma_1+e_{1i}\Sigma_2.
\]

\subsection{2. Most general first-order shell-compatible decomposition}

The most general decomposition of
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal X}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
into the shell-adapted basis is
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal X}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
&=
\hat n_\nu\hat n_i
\Big[
X_{\parallel\parallel}^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
X_{\parallel E}^{a}\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
X_{\parallel O}^{a}\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu e_{1i}
\Big[
X_{1\parallel}^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
X_{1E}^{a}\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
X_{1O}^{a}\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu e_{2i}
\Big[
X_{2\parallel}^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
X_{2E}^{a}\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
X_{2O}^{a}\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+e_{1\nu}\hat n_i
\Big[
Y_{1\parallel}^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
Y_{1E}^{a}\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
Y_{1O}^{a}\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+e_{2\nu}\hat n_i
\Big[
Y_{2\parallel}^{a}\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
Y_{2E}^{a}\,(\Sigma_1)_r
+
Y_{2O}^{a}\,(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+e_{1\nu}e_{1i}\Big[\cdots\Big]
+e_{1\nu}e_{2i}\Big[\cdots\Big]
+e_{2\nu}e_{1i}\Big[\cdots\Big]
+e_{2\nu}e_{2i}\Big[\cdots\Big].
\label{eq:full_tensor_decomp}
\end{align}

Here the scalar coefficients \(X_{\bullet}^{a},Y_{\bullet}^{a},\dots\) are functions of the local defect invariants and microscopic couplings.

\subsection{3. Minimal pieces relevant for the principal shell audit}

For the principal witness audit, not all terms in \eqref{eq:full_tensor_decomp} matter.
The shell projections \(c_\parallel,c_E,c_O\) only see the parts that survive contraction with
\[
\hat n^i\Sigma_3,\qquad
\frac12\bigl(e_1^i\Sigma_1+e_2^i\Sigma_2\bigr),\qquad
\frac12\bigl(-e_2^i\Sigma_1+e_1^i\Sigma_2\bigr).
\]

Therefore the minimal relevant decomposition is
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal X}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
&\simeq
\hat n_\nu\hat n_i\,X_{\parallel}^{a}(\Sigma_3)_r
+
\hat n_\nu e_{1i}\,X_{E1}^{a}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\hat n_\nu e_{2i}\,X_{E2}^{a}(\Sigma_2)_r
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu e_{1i}\,X_{O1}^{a}(\Sigma_2)_r
-
\hat n_\nu e_{2i}\,X_{O2}^{a}(\Sigma_1)_r
+\text{(null / irrelevant)}.
\label{eq:min_relevant_decomp}
\end{align}

This is the smallest shell-adapted tensor family that can feed all three witness channels.

\subsection{4. Specialization to \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}\)}

Because the pure \(JJ\) channel is already known to be axial-only at undifferentiated level, the natural minimal derivative ansatz for \(\widehat{\mathcal J}\) is
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
&\simeq
\hat n_\nu\hat n_i\,J_{\parallel}^{a}(\Sigma_3)_r
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu e_{1i}\,J_{O1}^{a}(\Sigma_2)_r
-\hat n_\nu e_{2i}\,J_{O2}^{a}(\Sigma_1)_r
+\text{(possible null terms)}.
\label{eq:dJ_min}
\end{align}

The important point is that derivative insertions can in principle unlock transverse Pauli structures even when the undifferentiated Hermitian \(JJ\) block is purely axial.

\subsection{5. Specialization to \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}\)}

The \(K\)-sector is already the natural transverse carrier at undifferentiated level, so its derivative decomposition should minimally include
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}_{i,r}{}^{a}(G_*;0)
&\simeq
\hat n_\nu e_{1i}\,K_{E1}^{a}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\hat n_\nu e_{2i}\,K_{E2}^{a}(\Sigma_2)_r
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu e_{1i}\,K_{O1}^{a}(\Sigma_2)_r
-\hat n_\nu e_{2i}\,K_{O2}^{a}(\Sigma_1)_r
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\hat n_\nu\hat n_i\,K_{\parallel}^{a}(\Sigma_3)_r
+\text{(null / irrelevant)}.
\label{eq:dK_min}
\end{align}

In the minimal explicit branch, one expects \(K_{\parallel}^{a}=0\) at leading order, but this is precisely one of the items that the derivative audit must check rather than assume.

\subsection{6. Induced structures in \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}\)}

Insert \eqref{eq:dJ_min} and \eqref{eq:dK_min} into
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})\widehat{\mathcal K}^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal J}(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})\widehat{\mathcal J}^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal K}(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})^\dagger
\Big].
\label{eq:dSigmaJK_repeat}
\end{align}

The key algebraic fact is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item undifferentiated \(\Sigma_3\)-with-\(\Sigma_{1,2}\) can cancel through anticommutation;
\item but derivative-generated shell tensors can reshuffle which shell-direction multiplies which Pauli matrix;
\item therefore the projected combinations \(c_E^{(JK)},c_O^{(JK)}\) need not vanish once \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}\) or \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}\) has nontrivial \(E/O\)-type components.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{7. Induced structures in \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}\)}

Likewise,
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
&=
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})\widehat{\mathcal K}^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal K}(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})^\dagger
\Big].
\label{eq:dSigmaKK_repeat}
\end{align}
Since both factors already carry transverse seed content, this block is the cleanest direct candidate for nonzero
\[
c_E^{(KK)},\qquad c_O^{(KK)}.
\]

\subsection{8. Explicit witness formulas in terms of derivative coefficients}

After shell-direction decomposition,
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{XY}
=
\hat n_\nu\,\mathcal S_{\parallel}^{(XY)}
+
e_{1\nu}\,\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}
+
e_{2\nu}\,\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)},
\qquad XY\in\{JK,KK\},
\]
with
\[
\mathcal S_{\bullet}^{(XY)}
=
s_{0,\bullet}^{(XY)}\mathbf 1_2
+
s_{1,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_1
+
s_{2,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_2
+
s_{3,\bullet}^{(XY)}\Sigma_3.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
c_E^{(XY)}
\propto
s_{1,1}^{(XY)}+s_{2,2}^{(XY)},
\label{eq:cE_in_s}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_O^{(XY)}
\propto
s_{2,1}^{(XY)}-s_{1,2}^{(XY)},
\label{eq:cO_in_s}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel^{(XY)}
\propto
s_{3,\parallel}^{(XY)}.
\label{eq:cpar_in_s}
\end{equation}

So the final derivative bookkeeping problem is reduced to computing the scalar coefficient sets
\[
s_{1,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,2}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{1,2}^{(JK)},
\]
and similarly for \(KK\).

\subsection{9. Honest endpoint of this step}

What is now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal allowed tensor basis for \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J}\) and \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K}\);
\item the exact way these enter \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}\) and \(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}\);
\item the shell witness projections \(c_E,c_O,c_\parallel\) in terms of the Pauli coefficients of the derivative self-energy blocks.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the explicit symbolic or numerical insertion of the final refined locked branch into the coefficients
\[
J_{\parallel}^{a},\ J_{O1}^{a},\ J_{O2}^{a},\ K_{E1}^{a},\ K_{E2}^{a},\ K_{O1}^{a},\ K_{O2}^{a},\ K_{\parallel}^{a}.
\]

\section{Final Eight-Scalar Reduction of the Transverse Microscopic Audit}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic transverse problem can be reduced to the Pauli coefficients of the shell-derivative self-energy blocks
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
\]

After shell-direction decomposition, only eight scalar coefficients matter for the transverse witness test.

\subsection{1. Shell-direction decomposition of the derivative self-energies}

For \(XY\in\{JK,KK\}\), write
\begin{equation}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{XY}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
=
\hat n_\nu\,\mathcal S_{\parallel}^{(XY)}
+
e_{1\nu}\,\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}
+
e_{2\nu}\,\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)}.
\label{eq:SXY_dir}
\end{equation}
Only \(\mathcal S_1^{(XY)}\) and \(\mathcal S_2^{(XY)}\) matter for the transverse sector.

Now Pauli-decompose:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{1}^{(XY)}
=
s_{0,1}^{(XY)}\mathbf 1_2
+
s_{1,1}^{(XY)}\Sigma_1
+
s_{2,1}^{(XY)}\Sigma_2
+
s_{3,1}^{(XY)}\Sigma_3,
\label{eq:S1_pauli}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{2}^{(XY)}
=
s_{0,2}^{(XY)}\mathbf 1_2
+
s_{1,2}^{(XY)}\Sigma_1
+
s_{2,2}^{(XY)}\Sigma_2
+
s_{3,2}^{(XY)}\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:S2_pauli}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Exact transverse witness formulas}

The shell-adapted witness projections are
\begin{equation}
c_E^{(XY)}
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal S_1^{(XY)})
+
\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal S_2^{(XY)})
\right],
\label{eq:cE_trace}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_O^{(XY)}
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal S_1^{(XY)})
-
\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal S_2^{(XY)})
\right].
\label{eq:cO_trace}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
\Tr(\Sigma_a\Sigma_b)=2\delta_{ab},
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(XY)}
\propto
s_{1,1}^{(XY)}+s_{2,2}^{(XY)},
}
\label{eq:cE_scalar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O^{(XY)}
\propto
s_{2,1}^{(XY)}-s_{1,2}^{(XY)}.
}
\label{eq:cO_scalar}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. The full transverse coefficients}

Therefore the full transverse shell coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
\propto
\bigl(s_{1,1}^{(JK)}+s_{2,2}^{(JK)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(s_{1,1}^{(KK)}+s_{2,2}^{(KK)}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:cE_full}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
\propto
\bigl(s_{2,1}^{(JK)}-s_{1,2}^{(JK)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(s_{2,1}^{(KK)}-s_{1,2}^{(KK)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:cO_full}
\end{equation}

So only the following eight numbers matter:
\[
s_{1,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,2}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{1,2}^{(JK)},
\qquad
s_{1,1}^{(KK)},\ s_{2,2}^{(KK)},\ s_{2,1}^{(KK)},\ s_{1,2}^{(KK)}.
\]

\subsection{4. Final yes/no criterion}

The transverse witness exists if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left(
\bigl[s_{1,1}^{(JK)}+s_{2,2}^{(JK)}\bigr]
+
\bigl[s_{1,1}^{(KK)}+s_{2,2}^{(KK)}\bigr],
\quad
\bigl[s_{2,1}^{(JK)}-s_{1,2}^{(JK)}\bigr]
+
\bigl[s_{2,1}^{(KK)}-s_{1,2}^{(KK)}\bigr]
\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:transverse_yesno}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Longitudinal coefficient remains separate}

The longitudinal piece is still
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel
=
c_\parallel^{(JJ)}+c_\parallel^{(JK)}+c_\parallel^{(KK)},
\label{eq:cpar_total_here}
\end{equation}
with the explicit seed dictionary
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_dict_here}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Honest endpoint}

At this stage, the remaining microscopic calculation is no longer conceptual and no longer infinite-dimensional in any practical sense.
It is the explicit symbolic or numerical computation of the eight Pauli coefficients in
\eqref{eq:cE_full}--\eqref{eq:cO_full}
from the chosen refined locked \(+\) Class II branch.

\section{Final Compression of the Transverse Audit to Two Fourier Overlaps}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The previous eight-scalar bookkeeping is correct as a completely general shell-derivative reduction.
However, inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II audit already isolated in the notes, the transverse problem compresses further to the two shell Fourier coefficients
\[
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]

Thus the actual remaining transverse problem is:
\[
\text{compute the first-shell Fourier overlaps generating }W^1,W^2.
\]

\subsection{1. Shell-level transverse matrices}

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the off-diagonal shell block is controlled by the \(Q=G_*\) primitive-cell Fourier coefficients.
The transverse Dirac matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Walpha_final}
\end{equation}
So the transverse witness problem is exactly the problem of computing
\[
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]

\subsection{2. Effective split}

Each transverse coefficient splits as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\qquad \alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Talpha_split_final}
\end{equation}
In the current refined locked isotropic/projector-stiffness route,
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)=0
\]
at quadratic order, because the direct projector-mixing source vanishes there.
Therefore the first genuinely nontrivial transverse shell matrices must come from
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\]
and/or its spectator renormalization. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{3. Explicit Class II transverse overlap formula}

For the Class II branch, the notes give the direct shell overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:Talpha_CII_overlap}
\end{equation}
This is the actual compressed form of the \(JK\)-driven transverse audit.

So the previous general derivative bookkeeping
\[
s_{1,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,2}^{(JK)},\ s_{2,1}^{(JK)},\ s_{1,2}^{(JK)},\dots
\]
is equivalent, in the explicit folded-Bragg realization, to the single Fourier convolution \eqref{eq:Talpha_CII_overlap}.

\subsection{4. Minimal first-shell-dominant channel}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant channel, the same formula reduces further to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto
iA_{G_*}\,(C_\alpha\!\cdot\! G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Talpha_minimal}
\end{equation}
Thus the transverse witness survives whenever the effective shell vectors \(C_1,C_2\) have nonzero projection on \(G_*\).

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0
\ \text{or}\
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:transverse_yesno_compressed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Relation to the reduced coefficients}

The reduced dictionary is still
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dict_again}
\end{equation}
Inside the folded-Bragg shell audit,
\[
c_E,\ c_O
\]
are just the shell-seed projections of
\[
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]
So the final transverse problem is no longer an uncontrolled operator question.
It is the finite Fourier-overlap computation of \(\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\).

\subsection{6. Honest endpoint}

At the most compressed explicit level currently justified by the notes, the remaining microscopic transverse frontier is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
\text{ from the Class II Fourier convolution \eqref{eq:Talpha_CII_overlap}.}
}
\label{eq:final_transverse_frontier}
\end{equation}

If one accepts the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction, this becomes the two-scalar test
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\! G_*),\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\! G_*).
\]
So the full transverse microscopic closure is reduced to two explicit shell Fourier overlaps.

\section{Final compressed transverse audit}

The remaining transverse microscopic problem is fully compressed to the shell Fourier coefficients
\[
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]

They split as
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
with
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)=0
\]
in the current refined locked quadratic route.

The explicit Class II shell overlap is
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
\]

In the minimal first-shell-dominant channel,
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\cdot G_*).
\]

Therefore the final transverse yes/no test is reduced to two explicit shell Fourier overlaps:
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*),\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*).
\]

\section{Final Audit Table for the Folded-Bragg Microscopic Closure}

The full folded-Bragg microscopic closure is reduced to the four shell quantities
