\section{TECT Final Audit Checklist (Closed vs Open)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic program is no longer broad.
It is a finite checklist.

There are two levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item shell-coefficient level;
\item full microscopic Dirac-stability audit level.
\end{enumerate}

The honest status is:
the transverse sector is already structurally realized,
while the real remaining frontier is the survival of the longitudinal primitive seed
inside the true full microscopic transport space.

\section{A. Shell-coefficient checklist}

The folded-Bragg shell bookkeeping is reduced to the four quantities
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel,\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*).
\]

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Quantity} & \text{Role} & \text{Status} \\
\hline
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*) &
\text{scalar shell offset} &
\text{bookkept, not load-bearing for nondegeneracy} \\
\hline
v_\parallel &
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0 \text{ witness} &
\textbf{open calibration / open actual survival} \\
\hline
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*) &
\alpha \text{ witness} &
\textbf{structurally realized; actual full extraction still open} \\
\hline
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*) &
\beta \text{ witness} &
\textbf{structurally realized; actual full extraction still open}
\end{array}
\]

The reduced dictionary remains
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

The decisive shell-level nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0
\ \text{or}\
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{B. Actual carrier-space checklist}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W\) be the actual shell-relevant microscopic transport space.

For any basis \(\{E_A\}\subset V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), define
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\]

Then the exact basis-level completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently, in shell-seed coordinates,
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,

\section{Actual Basis-Overlap Audit for the Longitudinal Primitive Seed}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic question is whether the full transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
contains at least one basis direction with nonzero overlap against the longitudinal shell target.

This is a finite linear-algebra problem.

\subsection{1. Longitudinal seed target}

The canonical primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\quad
N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=N^2_{ij}=0.
}
\label{eq:long_seed_target}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the corresponding shell covector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
}
\label{eq:Tparallel_target}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Microscopic basis decomposition}

Choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
of the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Decompose each basis tensor into the shell seed basis:
\begin{equation}
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp \mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\label{eq:EA_seed_decomp}
\end{equation}
Then the longitudinal overlap coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}
=
\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle
=
\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:lparA_muA}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal channel survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:exists_aA_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Explicit overlap formula}

Writing the microscopic basis tensors as \(E_{A,ij}^a\), one computes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}
=
\sum_{i,j,a}
(\hat n_i\hat n_j\delta_{a3})\,E_{A,ij}^a
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,E_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:lparA_explicit}
\end{equation}
Thus the practical audit is extremely simple:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{for each basis element }E_A,\ \text{compute }\hat n_i\hat n_jE_{A,ij}^{\,3}.
}
\label{eq:practical_long_audit}
\end{equation}

If at least one of these is nonzero, then the primitive longitudinal seed is embedded.

\subsection{4. Consequence for the reduced witness}

Because
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\label{eq:lambda_from_cpar_again}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
c_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\ \text{generically}.
}
\label{eq:lpar_generic_nonzero}
\end{equation}
So once one admissible longitudinal seed exists, the bad set is only a proper hyperplane in the finite carrier space. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection{5. Full audit criterion}

Together with the already-closed transverse half,
the complete microscopic carrier audit is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:full_basis_audit}
\end{equation}
But the current strongest honest status is that the transverse half is already structurally realized, so the real remaining check is only the first condition. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual remaining microscopic problem is the longitudinal basis-overlap audit.

\section{Closure of the Remaining Longitudinal Open Problem in the Current Complete LO Action}

\label{eq:current_LO_nondeg}
\end{equation}
This is already the exact reduced Dirac-type PDE statement for the current LO completion. 

\subsection{5. What is actually still open}

The remaining question is no longer:

\[
\text{``does the current LO action produce a longitudinal primitive channel?''}
\]

That is already answered: yes, through Branch B.

The real remaining microscopic question is instead:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the full complete TECT action contain an extra linear longitudinal tangent carrier}
\text{ beyond the current LO action class?}
}
\label{eq:real_remaining_open}
\end{equation}
If the answer is no, then the final theory stays on Branch B.
If the answer is yes, then Branch A becomes possible and must be re-audited explicitly. 

\section{Final Summary}

For the currently adopted complete lowest-order TECT realization, the longitudinal open problem is effectively closed:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi \Pi_Q = 0,
\qquad
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\]
so the first nonzero longitudinal traceless term is primitive:
\[
V^\mu_\parallel(\xi)\sim \theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Hence the solved lowest-order complete realization satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\]
so Branch B is forced in the present action class.

Thus the unresolved problem is no longer whether the current theory has a longitudinal channel.
It does.

The only remaining branch question is whether the true full complete TECT action contains an additional linear longitudinal tangent carrier not present in the current LO realization.

\section{Next Unfinished Step: Dynamical Closure of Chirality Protection via Mirror Lifting}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The topological index already forces a net chiral asymmetry, but this alone does not exclude vectorlike mirror pairs.
Therefore the next unfinished step is not to re-prove the index, but to close the dynamical mirror-lifting problem.

At the current note level, this problem has already been reduced to a finite-dimensional lifting theorem and, more sharply, to a single radial overlap test.

\subsection{1. What is already rigorous}

For the defect-sector twisted Dirac operator on the effective \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) background, the chiral asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
n_L-n_R
=
\sigma(Q_{\mathrm{def}})
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8}.
}
\label{eq:chi_index_recall}
\end{equation}
In particular, for the primitive positive twisting
\[
(q,m)=(1,1),
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Index}(D_+)=1.
}
\label{eq:index_one_recall}
\end{equation}
So at least one net protected chiral mode exists. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

In addition, the Callias theorem on the physical defect background gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Index}\,\mathcal D_\Phi=Q_{\mathrm{def}},
}
\label{eq:callias_recall}
\end{equation}
so \(Q_{\mathrm{def}}\neq 0\) guarantees at least one normalizable defect zero mode. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{2. What index theory does \emph{not} yet prove}

A nonzero index fixes only the \emph{difference}
\[
n_L-n_R=I.
\]
It does \emph{not} exclude the possibility of extra mirror pairs:
\begin{equation}
(n_L,n_R)=(I+r,r),\qquad r\ge 0.
\label{eq:index_not_enough}
\end{equation}
So index theory alone does not yet yield a purely chiral infrared spectrum. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Therefore the remaining unfinished chirality problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{can all vectorlike mirror pairs be lifted dynamically?}
}
\label{eq:remaining_mirror_problem}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Exact finite-dimensional mirror-lifting theorem}

Decompose the zero-mode space as
\begin{equation}
Z_L = Z_{\mathrm{top}} \oplus Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^L,
\qquad
Z_R = Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^R,
\label{eq:zero_mode_split}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\dim Z_{\mathrm{top}}=I,
\qquad
\dim Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^L=\dim Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^R=:r.
\]
Consider a chiral-odd self-adjoint operator on the zero-mode sector of the form
\begin{equation}
M
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & 0 & 0\\
0 & 0 & \mu^\dagger\\
0 & \mu & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:mirror_matrix}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mu:Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^L\to Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^R.
\]
If \(\mu\) is invertible, then:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{all mirror pairs are lifted, while the topological sector remains massless.}
}
\label{eq:mirror_lift_exact}
\end{equation}
Hence the infrared spectrum contains exactly \(I\) net protected chiral modes and no mirror zero modes. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection{4. Reduction to one scalar overlap test}

The notes sharpen this even further.
In the primitive channel, the projected mirror block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu(\Xi_f)=c(f)\,\mathbf 1_W,
}
\label{eq:mu_scalar_form}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\,\kappa(r)\,dr.
}
\label{eq:c_of_f}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\exists f:\ c(f)\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\mu(\Xi_f)\ \text{invertible}
\Longrightarrow
\text{full mirror lifting.}
}
\label{eq:kappa_nonzero_implies_lifting}
\end{equation}
Moreover, once \(c\not\equiv 0\), the set of allowed radial profiles with \(c(f)\neq 0\) is open and dense. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

So the unfinished dynamical chirality problem has been reduced to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0\ ? 
}
\label{eq:only_open_kappa}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Strongest honest current chirality statement}

Combining the rigorous parts already available, we obtain:

\paragraph{Theorem (current strongest honest chirality statement).}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the effective defect operator is the \(\mathrm{spin}^c\)-twisted \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) Dirac operator with
\[
\mathrm{Index}(D_+)=I>0;
\]
\item the physical defect background is Callias-admissible, so at least one normalizable localized zero mode exists;
\item the microscopic lifting-operator space contains one primitive channel with
\[
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then the TECT defect sector contains exactly \(I\) protected chiral infrared zero modes and no mirror zero modes.

\paragraph{Proof.}
By the index theorem, the net chiral asymmetry is \(I\). By Callias, there is a normalizable localized zero-mode sector on the physical defect. By \eqref{eq:kappa_nonzero_implies_lifting}, the mirror block \(\mu\) is invertible on the vectorlike mirror sector, so all mirror pairs are lifted. Therefore only the topological chiral sector remains massless, with multiplicity \(I\). \(\square\)

\subsection{6. What is closed and what is still open}

Closed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{index }+\text{ finite-dimensional mirror theorem }+\text{ radial-overlap reduction.}
}
\label{eq:closed_chi_parts}
\end{equation}

Still open:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive from the full microscopic TECT defect PDE an actual lifting channel with }\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:open_chi_part}
\end{equation}
The notes are explicit that this is the genuine remaining microscopic chirality problem. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\section{Final Summary}

The next unfinished step before a real Standard-Model theorem is not the topological index itself; that part is already done.

The true remaining chirality problem is the dynamical elimination of mirror pairs.

At the current strongest note level, this has been reduced to one scalar test:
\[
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0.
}
\]
If this holds for one physically realized primitive lifting channel, then:
\[
\text{index }I>0
\Longrightarrow
\text{net chiral sector}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mirror lifting}
\Longrightarrow
\text{exact protected chiral infrared spectrum of multiplicity }I.
\]

So the next genuinely useful calculation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct the microscopic primitive lifting operator and evaluate whether }\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0.
}
\]

\section{A Direct Sufficient Criterion for \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0\) in the Primitive Channel}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining unfinished chirality problem is whether the primitive lifting channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
\]
actually produces a nonzero radial overlap density \(\kappa(r)\).

Using the pointwise eigenspace decomposition of \(T(P)\), we can reduce this to a very explicit condition on the mirror wavefunctions.

\subsection{1. Radial overlap density}

The projected mirror scalar is
\begin{equation}
\mu(\Xi_f)=c(f)\,\mathbf 1_W,
\qquad
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\,\kappa(r)\,dr,
\label{eq:kappa_start}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)
=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}
\int_{S_r^2}
\big\langle
\psi_a^R(x),\,
\Gamma_\chi\otimes T(P(x))\,
\psi_a^L(x)
\big\rangle
\,d\Omega_r.
\label{eq:kappa_def}
\end{equation}
If \(\kappa\not\equiv 0\), then there exists a radial profile \(f\) such that \(c(f)\neq 0\), hence the mirror block is invertible and the full mirror sector is lifted. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{2. Primitive channel algebra}

Take
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3.
\label{eq:Tprimitive}
\end{equation}
Since \(P\) is a rank-one Hermitian projector, \(T(P)\) has eigenvalues
\[
2,-1,-1.
\]
Equivalently, with the orthogonal splitting
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
T(P)\big|_{\operatorname{im}P}=2\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
T(P)\big|_{\ker P}=-\,\mathbf 1.
\label{eq:T_action_split}
\end{equation}
This is already fixed in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{3. Pointwise decomposition of the mirror modes}

At each point \(x\), decompose the internal part of the mirror states into the projector line and its orthogonal complement:
\begin{equation}
\psi_a^L(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^L(x)+\eta_a^L(x),
\qquad
\psi_a^R(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^R(x)+\eta_a^R(x),
\label{eq:psi_split}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\eta_a^{L,R}(x)\in \ker P(x),
\qquad
z(x)^\dagger \eta_a^{L,R}(x)=0.
\]

Here \(\ell_a^{L,R}(x)\) are scalar chiral/spinor amplitudes after contracting the internal line \(\operatorname{im}P\).

\subsection{4. Exact decomposition of \(\kappa(r)\)}

Using \eqref{eq:T_action_split}, cross terms vanish by orthogonality between \(\operatorname{im}P\) and \(\ker P\), and we get
\begin{align}
\kappa(r)
&=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\Big[
2\,
\big\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\big\rangle
-
\big\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\big\rangle
\Big]
\,d\Omega_r
\nonumber\\
&=
2A(r)-B(r),
\label{eq:kappa_2AminusB}
\end{align}
where
\begin{equation}
A(r):=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\big\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\big\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\label{eq:Aofr}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r):=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\big\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\big\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\label{eq:Bofr}
\end{equation}

So the primitive-channel radial overlap is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r).
}
\label{eq:kappa_main_formula}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Immediate sufficient criterion}

Therefore \(\kappa(r)\equiv 0\) would require the identity
\begin{equation}
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad\text{for all }r>0.
\label{eq:fine_tuned_cancel}
\end{equation}
Hence we obtain the following exact sufficient criterion:

\paragraph{Proposition.}
If there exists one radius \(r_0>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
2A(r_0)\neq B(r_0),
\label{eq:suff_nonzero_point}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:kappa_not_zero_conclusion}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Proof.}
By \eqref{eq:kappa_main_formula},
\[
\kappa(r_0)=2A(r_0)-B(r_0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\kappa\) is not the zero function. \(\square\)

\subsection{6. Physical interpretation}

Equation \eqref{eq:kappa_main_formula} shows that the primitive channel \(T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3\) does not treat the projector line and the orthogonal doublet symmetrically:
the line contribution enters with weight \(+2\), while the orthogonal complement enters with weight \(-1\).

Therefore exact vanishing of \(\kappa(r)\) requires a highly constrained cancellation between:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the line-overlap channel \(A(r)\),
\item the orthogonal-doublet overlap channel \(B(r)\).
\end{enumerate}

This means that, unless there is an exact hidden symmetry of the full microscopic defect PDE forcing
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\quad\forall r,
\]
the primitive channel is expected to yield \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0\).

\subsection{7. Honest limit of the argument}

What this proves:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the mirror-lifting problem is reduced to checking whether an exact functional cancellation }2A(r)=B(r)\text{ is forced.}
}
\label{eq:honest_limit_1}
\end{equation}

What this does \emph{not} yet prove:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{from the full microscopic TECT defect PDE alone, without extra input, that such a cancellation is impossible.}
}
\label{eq:honest_limit_2}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic chirality problem is now sharpened to the following:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete defect PDE possess a hidden symmetry enforcing }2A(r)=B(r)\text{ identically?}
}
\label{eq:hidden_symmetry_question}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

For the primitive internal lifting channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3,
\]
the radial overlap density decomposes exactly as
\[
\boxed{
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r),
}
\]
where \(A(r)\) is the projector-line overlap and \(B(r)\) is the orthogonal-doublet overlap.

Hence a completely explicit sufficient criterion for mirror lifting is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists r_0>0:\ 2A(r_0)\neq B(r_0)
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{full mirror lifting.}
}
\]

Thus the unresolved microscopic question is no longer abstract.
It is whether the full TECT defect dynamics enforces an exact cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\quad\forall r,
\]
or whether the primitive channel is genuinely active.

\section{Sharpened Dynamical Chirality Closure: Reduction to Exact Functional Cancellation}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining dynamical chirality problem is no longer broad.
It has been reduced to one explicit functional question:
does the full defect PDE force the exact cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0?
\]

If not, then the primitive mirror-lifting channel is active and mirror pairs are lifted.

\subsection{1. Exact mirror-lifting reduction already closed}

For a defect-localized chiral-odd operator
\[
\Xi_f=f(r)\,\Gamma_\chi\otimes T(P),
\]
the mirror block has the exact form
\begin{equation}
\mu(\Xi_f)=c(f)\,\mathbf 1_W,
\qquad
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\,\kappa(r)\,dr.
\label{eq:mu_c_kappa_recall}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa\not\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\exists f:\ c(f)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\mu(\Xi_f)\ \text{invertible}
\Longrightarrow
\text{all mirror pairs are lifted.}
}
\label{eq:kappa_implies_lift_recall}
\end{equation}
This is already exact. 

\subsection{2. Primitive internal channel}

Take the canonical primitive channel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3.
}
\label{eq:Tprimitive_recall}
\end{equation}
Since \(P\) is a rank-one Hermitian projector, \(T(P)\) has eigenvalues
\[
2,-1,-1,
\]
so it is pointwise invertible and sharply distinguishes the projector line and the orthogonal doublet. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{3. Exact decomposition of the radial overlap}

Decompose the internal parts of the mirror states at each point into the projector line and its orthogonal complement:
\[
\psi_a^{L,R}=z\,\ell_a^{L,R}+\eta_a^{L,R},
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}\in \ker P,
\qquad
z^\dagger\eta_a^{L,R}=0.
\]
Then, by the eigenspace action of \(T(P)\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r),
}
\label{eq:kappa_2AminusB_recall}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\label{eq:A_r_recall}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\label{eq:B_r_recall}
\end{equation}

Thus exact vanishing of \(\kappa\) is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0.
}
\label{eq:exact_cancel_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Immediate sufficient criterion}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists r_0>0:\ 2A(r_0)\neq B(r_0)
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:sufficient_nonzero_again}
\end{equation}
So full mirror lifting follows from failure of the exact cancellation at even one radius.

\subsection{5. What would be needed for \(\kappa\equiv0\)}

For \(\kappa(r)\equiv0\) to hold identically, the full microscopic defect dynamics must impose a hidden constraint strong enough to force
\[
2A(r)=B(r)
\]
for every radius.

This is much stronger than:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a single integral cancellation,
\item a pointwise sign change,
\item or accidental zero at isolated radii.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the remaining microscopic obstruction to mirror lifting is not generic cancellation but an exact functional symmetry:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{hidden PDE symmetry } \Longrightarrow 2A(r)=B(r)\ \forall r.
}
\label{eq:hidden_symmetry_required}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Strongest honest current conclusion}

The strongest honest statement now is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The dynamical chirality problem has been reduced to ruling out an exact cancellation symmetry }2A(r)=B(r)\ \forall r.
}
\label{eq:strongest_honest_chi}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{unless the full microscopic defect PDE enforces }2A(r)=B(r)\ \forall r,
\text{ the primitive channel generically yields }\kappa\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:generic_kappa_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{7. Consequence for the protected chiral spectrum}

Once \(\kappa\not\equiv0\) is established for one realized primitive lifting channel,
the chain is complete:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Index}(D_+)=I>0
\Longrightarrow
\text{net chiral asymmetry}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mirror lifting}
\Longrightarrow
\text{exact protected chiral infrared spectrum of multiplicity }I.
}
\label{eq:full_chiral_chain}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining dynamical chirality question is no longer “is mirror lifting imaginable?”
That part is already solved.

For the primitive channel \(T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3\), the radial overlap density is exactly
\[
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r).
\]
Therefore mirror lifting fails only if the full defect dynamics enforces the exact functional identity
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0.
\]

So the remaining microscopic frontier is now maximally sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete TECT defect PDE possess a hidden symmetry forcing }2A(r)=B(r)\ \forall r?
}
\]

If the answer is no, then generically \(\kappa\not\equiv0\), the mirror sector is lifted, and chirality protection is dynamically closed.

\section{Leading-Asymptotic Criterion for Nonvanishing of \(\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining mirror-lifting question can be reduced to a boundary-asymptotic test.
If the leading asymptotics of \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) fail to satisfy the exact matching condition
\[
2A(r)=B(r)
\]
near either \(r\to0\) or \(r\to\infty\), then \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv0\).

So the practical microscopic task is not the full function first, but the leading asymptotic coefficients and exponents.

\subsection{1. Primitive-channel overlap decomposition}

For the primitive internal channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3,
\]
the radial overlap density is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r),
}
\label{eq:kappa_AB_recall}
\end{equation}
with \(A(r)\) the projector-line overlap and \(B(r)\) the orthogonal-doublet overlap. 

Therefore mirror lifting fails only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0.
}
\label{eq:exact_cancel_recall}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Core asymptotics}

Let the relevant defect ansatz be radial, with profile \(f(r)\), as in the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) hedgehog/lump construction. 

Decompose the mirror wavefunctions near the core as
\[
\psi_a^{L,R}(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^{L,R}(x)+\eta_a^{L,R}(x),
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}\in\ker P(x).
\]
Assume the leading core asymptotics
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{m_{L,R}},
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{n_{L,R}},
\label{eq:core_modes}
\end{equation}
with nonnegative exponents \(m_{L,R},n_{L,R}\).

Then the sphere measure contributes \(r^2 d\Omega\), so
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_0\,r^{2+m_L+m_R},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_0\,r^{2+n_L+n_R},
\qquad
(r\to0),
\label{eq:AB_core_asym}
\end{equation}
where
\[
a_0=\sum_a\int_{S^2}\langle zL_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(zL_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega,
\qquad
b_0=\sum_a\int_{S^2}\langle H_a^R,\Gamma_\chi H_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega.
\]

Hence:

\paragraph{Core noncancellation criterion.}
If
\begin{equation}
m_L+m_R\neq n_L+n_R,
\label{eq:core_power_mismatch}
\end{equation}
then \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different leading powers as \(r\to0\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:core_power_implies_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Even if the powers match, if
\begin{equation}
2a_0\neq b_0,
\label{eq:core_coeff_mismatch}
\end{equation}
then again
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0
\quad\text{already at leading core order.}
}
\label{eq:core_coeff_implies_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Far-field asymptotics}

For a localized Callias-admissible defect background, the zero modes are exponentially localized. 
So assume
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim \widetilde L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-\mu_{L,R}r},
\label{eq:far_line}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim \widetilde H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-\nu_{L,R}r},
\label{eq:far_doublet}
\end{equation}
with \(\mu_{L,R},\nu_{L,R}>0\).

Then
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{2+\alpha_L+\alpha_R}e^{-(\mu_L+\mu_R)r},
\label{eq:A_far}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{2+\beta_L+\beta_R}e^{-(\nu_L+\nu_R)r},
\label{eq:B_far}
\end{equation}
as \(r\to\infty\).

Hence:

\paragraph{Far-field noncancellation criterion.}
If
\begin{equation}
\mu_L+\mu_R\neq \nu_L+\nu_R,
\label{eq:far_exp_mismatch}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\alpha_L+\alpha_R\neq \beta_L+\beta_R,
\label{eq:far_power_mismatch}
\end{equation}
then \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different leading asymptotics at infinity, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:far_mismatch_implies_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Even when the decay rates and powers match, if
\begin{equation}
2a_\infty\neq b_\infty,
\label{eq:far_coeff_mismatch}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0
\quad\text{already at leading far-field order.}
}
\label{eq:far_coeff_implies_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Exact cancellation requires simultaneous matching at both ends}

Combining the previous two steps, exact functional cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0
\]
requires, at minimum:

\begin{enumerate}
\item matching leading core powers,
\item matching leading core coefficients,
\item matching leading far-field decay exponents,
\item matching leading far-field powers,
\item matching leading far-field coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{exact cancellation requires simultaneous asymptotic matching at both }r\to0\text{ and }r\to\infty.
}
\label{eq:both_ends_matching}
\end{equation}

This is far stronger than any symmetry statement currently proved in the notes, because the known \(U(2)\) structure does not force equality between the line-overlap channel and the doublet-overlap channel. 

\subsection{5. Practical sufficient criterion}

So the practical final sufficient criterion for mirror lifting is:

\paragraph{Proposition.}
Suppose that for the physically relevant defect ansatz,
either

\begin{equation}
(m_L+m_R)\neq (n_L+n_R),
\label{eq:practical_cond1}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
2a_0\neq b_0,
\label{eq:practical_cond2}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
(\mu_L+\mu_R,\alpha_L+\alpha_R)\neq(\nu_L+\nu_R,\beta_L+\beta_R),
\label{eq:practical_cond3}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
2a_\infty\neq b_\infty.
\label{eq:practical_cond4}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:kappa_nonzero_practical}
\end{equation}

Consequently there exists a radial profile \(f\) with
\[
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\kappa(r)\,dr\neq 0,
\]
and the mirror block is invertible.

\subsection{6. Honest remaining microscopic task}

What remains genuinely open is not the logic above.
It is the explicit extraction of
\[
m_{L,R},\ n_{L,R},\ a_0,\ b_0,\ \mu_{L,R},\ \nu_{L,R},\ a_\infty,\ b_\infty
\]
from the full microscopic TECT defect PDE for the relevant defect background.

So the next nonredundant calculation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the core and far-field asymptotics of the line sector } \ell_a^{L,R}
\text{ and the doublet sector }\eta_a^{L,R}.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The mirror-lifting obstruction has been reduced to the exact cancellation condition
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0.
\]

A practical sufficient criterion for ruling this out is any asymptotic mismatch between \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) at either boundary:

\[
\text{core power mismatch,}
\quad
\text{core coefficient mismatch,}
\quad
\text{far-field decay mismatch,}
\quad
\text{far-field coefficient mismatch.}
\]

If any one of these occurs, then
\[
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0,
\]
hence some natural primitive lifting operator has nonzero projected mirror coupling, and the full mirror sector is lifted.

Therefore the remaining microscopic task is now completely concrete:
compute the leading asymptotics of the projector-line and orthogonal-doublet mirror components in the relevant full TECT defect PDE.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Far-Field Sufficient Criterion for \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The canonical Callias pair already gives an asymptotic mass splitting between the projector line and its orthogonal doublet.
If the actual defect PDE respects this asymptotic eigenspace splitting, then the two overlap channels \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) decay with different exponential rates at infinity.
That alone rules out the exact cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r.
\]

\subsection{1. Canonical asymptotic data from the Callias pair}

For a smooth \(\mathbb{CP}^2\)-projector defect \(P(x)\), define
\begin{equation}
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],
\qquad
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3),
\qquad
\mu\neq 0.
\label{eq:callias_pair_far}
\end{equation}
The notes establish that
\begin{equation}
D_i\Phi=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}\Phi=\{2\mu,-\mu,-\mu\},
\qquad
\Phi^2\ge \mu^2\mathbf 1_3,
\label{eq:phi_spectrum_far}
\end{equation}
and therefore \((A,\Phi)\) is Callias-admissible. Any defect zero mode is exponentially localized. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

Thus the internal bundle splits asymptotically into the \(\Phi\)-eigenspaces
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus \ker P,
\]
with masses \(2|\mu|\) on the line \(\operatorname{im}P\) and \(|\mu|\) on the orthogonal doublet \(\ker P\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{2. Asymptotic decomposition of mirror modes}

Decompose the mirror modes as
\begin{equation}
\psi_a^{L,R}(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^{L,R}(x)+\eta_a^{L,R}(x),
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}(x)\in \ker P(x),
\label{eq:mirror_split_far}
\end{equation}
with \(z(x)\) spanning \(\operatorname{im}P(x)\).

Assume the actual defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the same Callias pair \((A,\Phi)\), so that the line component and orthogonal-doublet component follow the corresponding asymptotic mass scales.
Then their far-field behavior has the form
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)
\sim
L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\label{eq:ell_far}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)
\sim
H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-|\mu|r},
\label{eq:eta_far}
\end{equation}
for some angular spinors \(L_a^{L,R},H_a^{L,R}\). This is the natural asymptotic form compatible with the spectral gap in \eqref{eq:phi_spectrum_far}. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection{3. Far-field asymptotics of \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\)}

Recall
\begin{equation}
A(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\label{eq:A_far_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}\int_{S_r^2}
\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\label{eq:B_far_def}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:ell_far}--\eqref{eq:eta_far}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{2+\alpha_L+\alpha_R}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
r\to\infty,
\label{eq:A_far_asym}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{2+\beta_L+\beta_R}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad
r\to\infty,
\label{eq:B_far_asym}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\infty=
\sum_a\int_{S^2}\langle zL_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(zL_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega,
\qquad
b_\infty=
\sum_a\int_{S^2}\langle H_a^R,\Gamma_\chi H_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega.
\]

\subsection{4. Immediate consequence}

If both asymptotic coefficients are nonzero,
\begin{equation}
a_\infty\neq 0,
\qquad
b_\infty\neq 0,
\label{eq:both_nonzero_far}
\end{equation}
then \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different exponential decay rates:
\[
A(r)\sim e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r}.
\]
Therefore they cannot satisfy
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r
\]
identically.

Hence we obtain:

\paragraph{Proposition.}
Assume the actual relevant defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the canonical Callias pair
\((A,\Phi)\) with \(\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf1_3)\), and that both the line-overlap and orthogonal-doublet overlap channels are asymptotically nontrivial:
\[
a_\infty\neq 0,\qquad b_\infty\neq 0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:kappa_nonzero_far_prop}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Proof.}
By \eqref{eq:A_far_asym} and \eqref{eq:B_far_asym}, \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different leading exponential rates at infinity. Therefore the identity \(2A(r)=B(r)\) cannot hold for all sufficiently large \(r\), and hence cannot hold for all \(r>0\). So \(\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\) is not the zero function. \(\square\)

\subsection{5. What remains open}

This does \emph{not} yet prove that
\[
a_\infty\neq 0,\qquad b_\infty\neq 0
\]
for the true full microscopic TECT defect PDE.

So the genuine remaining task is now sharpened to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{show that the actual mirror-sector asymptotics has nonzero support in both }
\operatorname{im}P
\text{ and }
\ker P.
}
\label{eq:remaining_support_task}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, one must derive from the full defect PDE that the asymptotic amplitudes \(L_a^{L,R}\) and \(H_a^{L,R}\) do not vanish identically in the physically relevant primitive lifting channel.

\section{Final Summary}

For the canonical primitive channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3,
\]
the Callias Higgs field has asymptotic eigenvalues
\[
2\mu,-\mu,-\mu.
\]
Hence, if the true defect PDE follows this asymptotic channel splitting, then the projector-line overlap and orthogonal-doublet overlap behave as
\[
A(r)\sim a_\infty r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r}.
\]
Therefore, if
\[
a_\infty\neq 0,\qquad b_\infty\neq 0,
\]
the exact cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r
\]
is impossible, and so
\[
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic chirality problem has been reduced further:
not to a general hidden symmetry question anymore, but to checking whether the actual defect mirror modes have asymptotically nonzero support in both the line and doublet sectors.

\section{Far-Field Asymptotic Splitting Criterion for Mirror Lifting}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The remaining dynamical chirality problem is to decide whether
\[
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)
\]
can vanish identically.

At the current rigorous level, the sharpest usable result is a far-field criterion:
if the actual defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the canonical Callias pair
\[
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],\qquad \Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3),
\]
and if the mirror mode has nonzero asymptotic support in both the projector-line sector and the orthogonal-doublet sector, then \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv0\).

\subsection{1. Canonical Callias asymptotics}

For a smooth projector defect \(P:\mathbb R^3\to\mathbb{CP}^2\), define
\begin{equation}
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],\qquad
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3),\qquad \mu\neq0.
\end{equation}
The notes establish:
\begin{equation}
D_i\Phi=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}\Phi=\{2\mu,-\mu,-\mu\},
\qquad
\Phi^2\ge \mu^2\mathbf 1_3.
\end{equation}
Hence the pair is Callias-admissible and defect zero modes are exponentially localized. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

Therefore the internal bundle splits asymptotically as
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P,
\]
with asymptotic mass scales
\[
2|\mu|\quad\text{on }\operatorname{im}P,
\qquad
|\mu|\quad\text{on }\ker P.
\]

\subsection{2. Mirror-mode decomposition}

Decompose the mirror states pointwise as
\begin{equation}
\psi_a^{L,R}(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^{L,R}(x)+\eta_a^{L,R}(x),
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}(x)\in\ker P(x),
\end{equation}
where \(z(x)\) spans \(\operatorname{im}P(x)\).

Then the primitive overlap density is
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
A(r)=\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)=\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\end{equation}
This reduction is already exact. 

\subsection{3. Far-field asymptotics}

Assume the actual defect PDE approaches the same Callias asymptotic operator.
Then the line and doublet sectors inherit the asymptotic decay scales:
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-|\mu|r}.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{2+\alpha_L+\alpha_R}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad r\to\infty,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{2+\beta_L+\beta_R}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad r\to\infty.
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Immediate noncancellation theorem}

Suppose
\begin{equation}
a_\infty\neq 0,
\qquad
b_\infty\neq 0.
\end{equation}
Then \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different leading exponential decay rates:
\[
A(r)\sim e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r}.
\]
Therefore the identity
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0
\]
is impossible.

So we obtain:

\paragraph{Theorem.}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual far-field defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the canonical Callias pair \((A,\Phi)\) with \(\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3)\);
\item the asymptotic mirror mode has nonzero support in both sectors:
\[
a_\infty\neq0,\qquad b_\infty\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\end{equation}
Consequently there exists an allowed radial profile \(f\) such that
\[
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\kappa(r)\,dr\neq0,
\]
so the projected mirror block is invertible and the full mirror sector is lifted.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Different exponential rates at infinity forbid the exact functional identity \(2A(r)=B(r)\) for all sufficiently large \(r\). Therefore \(\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\) cannot vanish identically. Since \(\mu(\Xi_f)=c(f)\mathbf 1_W\), nonzero \(c(f)\) implies full-rank mirror lifting. \(\square\)

\subsection{5. What is still open}

This does not yet prove, from the full microscopic TECT defect PDE alone, that
\[
a_\infty\neq0,\qquad b_\infty\neq0.
\]
So the actual remaining microscopic task is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive from the full defect PDE that the asymptotic mirror mode has nonzero support in both }
\operatorname{im}P
\text{ and }
\ker P.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The canonical primitive channel already provides an asymptotic mass splitting
\[
2|\mu| \quad \text{vs.}\quad |\mu|
\]
between the projector-line sector and the orthogonal-doublet sector. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Therefore, if the actual defect PDE follows this asymptotic splitting and the mirror mode has nonzero support in both sectors, then
\[
A(r)\sim e^{-4|\mu|r},\qquad B(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r},
\]
so exact cancellation
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad\forall r
\]
is impossible.

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0,
}
\]
and mirror lifting follows.

So the remaining unfinished chirality step is now maximally concrete:
\[
\boxed{
\text{show that the actual asymptotic mirror mode occupies both }\operatorname{im}P\text{ and }\ker P.
}
\]

\section{Far-field reduction of the remaining mirror-lifting problem}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining dynamical chirality problem is no longer to understand the full function \(\kappa(r)\) from scratch.
It is enough to determine whether the actual asymptotic mirror mode has nonzero support in both asymptotic eigensectors of the primitive Callias Higgs field.

\subsection{1. Canonical asymptotic splitting}

For the primitive Callias pair
\begin{equation}
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],
\qquad
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3),
\qquad \mu\neq 0,
\end{equation}
the asymptotic spectral data are
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\Phi=\{2\mu,-\mu,-\mu\},
\qquad
\Phi^2\ge \mu^2\mathbf 1_3.
\end{equation}
Hence the internal bundle splits asymptotically as
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P
\]
with distinct absolute mass scales
\[
2|\mu| \quad \text{on } \operatorname{im}P,
\qquad
|\mu| \quad \text{on } \ker P.
\]

\subsection{2. Mirror-mode asymptotic decomposition}

Write the mirror modes as
\begin{equation}
\psi_a^{L,R}=z\,\ell_a^{L,R}+\eta_a^{L,R},
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}\in\ker P,
\end{equation}
where \(z\) spans \(\operatorname{im}P\).

If the actual defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the same Callias pair, then the two components have the far-field form
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-|\mu|r}.
\end{equation}

Therefore the overlap channels satisfy
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad r\to\infty.
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Sharp sufficient criterion}

If
\begin{equation}
a_\infty\neq 0,
\qquad
b_\infty\neq 0,
\end{equation}
then \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\) have different leading exponential decay rates, so the exact identity
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0
\]
is impossible.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\infty\neq 0,\quad b_\infty\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{full mirror lifting.}
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. What is still genuinely open}

The only remaining microscopic issue is whether the actual asymptotic mirror mode has nonzero support in both sectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\infty\neq 0\ ?,
\qquad
b_\infty\neq 0\ ?.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:
does the true defect PDE asymptotic solution occupy both \(\operatorname{im}P\) and \(\ker P\), rather than collapsing entirely into one sector?

\section{Final Summary}

The mirror-lifting problem is now reduced to a two-number far-field support test.

Once the asymptotic mirror mode has nonzero support in both the projector line and the orthogonal doublet, the primitive overlap channels decay as
\[
A(r)\sim e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r},
\]
so exact cancellation is impossible and \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv0\).

Thus the remaining unfinished chirality step is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive from the actual defect PDE whether }a_\infty\neq 0\text{ and }b_\infty\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Sharpened Far-Field Criterion for \(\kappa(r)\not\equiv0\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The previous sufficient condition
\[
a_\infty\neq0,\qquad b_\infty\neq0
\]
was stronger than necessary.

Because the primitive Callias channel has different asymptotic decay scales on
\(\operatorname{im}P\) and \(\ker P\), it is enough that at least one of the two leading asymptotic overlap coefficients be nonzero.

\subsection{1. Primitive channel and asymptotic splitting}

In the primitive channel
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3,
\label{eq:primitive_T_again}
\end{equation}
the projector-line and orthogonal-doublet sectors are distinguished by
\[
T(P)|_{\operatorname{im}P}=2\,\mathbf1,
\qquad
T(P)|_{\ker P}=-\,\mathbf1.
\]
For the canonical Callias Higgs field
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf1_3),
\label{eq:Phi_again}
\end{equation}
the asymptotic absolute mass scales are
\[
2|\mu|\quad\text{on }\operatorname{im}P,
\qquad
|\mu|\quad\text{on }\ker P.
\]
The mirror modes are exponentially localized. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2} :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{2. Far-field asymptotics}

Decompose the mirror modes as
\[
\psi_a^{L,R}=z\,\ell_a^{L,R}+\eta_a^{L,R},
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}\in\ker P.
\]
Assume the actual defect PDE is asymptotically governed by the same Callias pair. Then
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\label{eq:ell_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-|\mu|r}.
\label{eq:eta_again}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad
r\to\infty,
\label{eq:A_B_far_again}
\end{equation}
for suitable integers \(m,n\).

\subsection{3. Sharpened asymptotic criterion}

Recall
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r).
\label{eq:kappa_again}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case 1: \(b_\infty\neq0\).}
Since \(e^{-2|\mu|r}\) decays slower than \(e^{-4|\mu|r}\),
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)
=
2A(r)-B(r)
\sim
-\,b_\infty\,r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad r\to\infty.
\label{eq:kappa_case1}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_\infty\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:binfty_nonzero_implies}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case 2: \(b_\infty=0\) but \(a_\infty\neq0\).}
Then the first surviving far-field term is
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)\sim 2a_\infty\,r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad r\to\infty,
\label{eq:kappa_case2}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\infty\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:ainfty_nonzero_implies}
\end{equation}

Combining both:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:main_sharpened_far}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. What exact cancellation would now require}

Therefore the exact identity
\[
2A(r)=B(r)\qquad \forall r>0
\]
can survive the far-field test only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\infty=0,
\qquad
b_\infty=0.
}
\label{eq:both_zero_needed}
\end{equation}
That is, the primitive bilinear pairing must vanish asymptotically in both the line channel and the doublet channel.

So the remaining obstruction is no longer “matching two nonzero exponentials.”
It is the much stronger statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual asymptotic primitive pairing vanishes identically in both sectors.}
}
\label{eq:strong_obstruction}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Consequence for mirror lifting}

Once \((a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0)\), one has \(\kappa\not\equiv0\).
Then the finite-dimensional mirror theorem yields
\[
\exists f:\ c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\kappa(r)\,dr\neq0,
\]
and therefore the projected mirror block is invertible and the full mirror sector is lifted. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{Final Summary}

For the primitive channel \(T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3\), the far-field overlap channels have different decay rates:
\[
A(r)\sim a_\infty r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r}.
\]

Therefore the correct sharpened sufficient condition is not
\[
a_\infty\neq0 \text{ and } b_\infty\neq0,
\]
but simply
\[
\boxed{
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

Indeed:
\[
b_\infty\neq0 \Longrightarrow \kappa(r)\sim -B(r)\neq0,
\]
and if \(b_\infty=0\) but \(a_\infty\neq0\), then
\[
\kappa(r)\sim 2A(r)\neq0.
\]

So the remaining microscopic chirality task is now maximally reduced:
\[
\boxed{
\text{show that the actual asymptotic primitive pairing is not identically zero in both sectors at once.}
}
\]

\section{Far-Field Mode Equation and the Reduction of the Remaining Chirality Problem}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The canonical Callias pair already fixes the asymptotic eigenspace splitting of the internal bundle:
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P,
\]
with asymptotic mass scales \(2|\mu|\) and \(|\mu|\).
Therefore the far-field mode equation splits into two decoupled asymptotic sectors.
The coefficients \(a_\infty\) and \(b_\infty\) are not determined by the asymptotic operator itself; they are matching data fixed by the global defect solution.

Hence the remaining chirality problem is no longer a far-field spectral problem.
It is a core-to-infinity matching problem.

\subsection{1. Canonical asymptotic operator}

For
\begin{equation}
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],\qquad
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf1_3),
\qquad \mu\neq0,
\end{equation}
the notes establish
\begin{equation}
D_i\Phi=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}\Phi=\{2\mu,-\mu,-\mu\},
\qquad
\Phi^2\ge \mu^2\mathbf1_3.
\end{equation}
Therefore the asymptotic internal bundle splits as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P,
\end{equation}
with distinct absolute mass scales
\begin{equation}
2|\mu|
\quad\text{on }\operatorname{im}P,
\qquad
|\mu|
\quad\text{on }\ker P.
\end{equation}
This is already closed. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsection{2. Far-field mode decomposition}

Write the mirror modes as
\begin{equation}
\psi_a^{L,R}(x)=z(x)\,\ell_a^{L,R}(x)+\eta_a^{L,R}(x),
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}(x)\in\ker P(x),
\end{equation}
where \(z(x)\) spans \(\operatorname{im}P(x)\).

Because the asymptotic Higgs field is diagonal on this splitting, the far-field equation decouples at leading order into a line equation and a doublet equation.
Therefore the leading asymptotic solutions have the form
\begin{equation}
\ell_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim L_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\alpha_{L,R}}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\label{eq:ell_far_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_a^{L,R}(r,\Omega)\sim H_a^{L,R}(\Omega)\,r^{\beta_{L,R}}e^{-|\mu|r}.
\label{eq:eta_far_final}
\end{equation}

The crucial point is that the asymptotic operator fixes the \emph{rates}
\[
2|\mu|,\qquad |\mu|,
\]
but not the amplitudes \(L_a^{L,R}\) and \(H_a^{L,R}\).
Those are determined by global matching to the interior defect solution.

\subsection{3. Consequence for \(A(r)\) and \(B(r)\)}

The primitive overlap channels are
\begin{equation}
A(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(r)=
\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:ell_far_final}--\eqref{eq:eta_far_final}, one gets
\begin{equation}
A(r)\sim a_\infty\,r^{m}e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty\,r^{n}e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad
r\to\infty,
\end{equation}
for some integers \(m,n\).

Hence
\begin{equation}
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0.
\end{equation}
This is the sharpened far-field criterion obtained previously.

\subsection{4. What the asymptotic problem does and does not decide}

The far-field operator determines:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the sector splitting \(\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P\),
\item the unequal decay rates \(2|\mu|\) and \(|\mu|\),
\item the fact that exact cancellation \(2A=B\) is impossible unless both asymptotic amplitudes vanish.
\end{enumerate}

But it does \emph{not} determine by itself:
\begin{equation}
a_\infty=0\ ?,
\qquad
b_\infty=0\ ?.
\end{equation}
Those are not spectral invariants of the asymptotic operator.
They are global matching data fixed by the full defect PDE.

\subsection{5. Sharpened honest conclusion}

Therefore the remaining chirality problem is no longer:
\[
\text{``what is the far-field decay rate?''}
\]
That is already known.

It is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the global defect solution match onto the far-field with }
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0)?
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the only remaining microscopic obstruction to mirror lifting is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full defect PDE forces both asymptotic primitive pairings to vanish simultaneously.}
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Why this is now a core-matching problem}

Since the asymptotic equations leave \(L_a^{L,R}\) and \(H_a^{L,R}\) as integration constants, the values of \(a_\infty\) and \(b_\infty\) are set by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the regularity condition at the defect core,
\item the global transport through the intermediate region,
\item the matching to the decaying asymptotic solutions.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the remaining microscopic task is not asymptotic diagonalization but core-to-infinity matching in the full defect PDE.

\section{Final Summary}

The canonical Callias pair fixes the far-field splitting and decay rates:
\[
\operatorname{im}P:\ e^{-2|\mu|r},
\qquad
\ker P:\ e^{-|\mu|r}.
\]
Therefore the primitive overlap channels satisfy
\[
A(r)\sim a_\infty r^m e^{-4|\mu|r},
\qquad
B(r)\sim b_\infty r^n e^{-2|\mu|r}.
\]

So if
\[
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0),
\]
then
\[
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r)\not\equiv0,
\]
and mirror lifting follows.

What the far-field operator does \emph{not} decide is whether
\[
a_\infty=0,\qquad b_\infty=0
\]
for the actual microscopic defect solution.
Those are global matching coefficients.

Thus the remaining unfinished chirality step is now maximally sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{solve the core-to-infinity matching problem for the actual defect PDE and determine whether }
(a_\infty,b_\infty)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

\section{Core-to-Infinity Matching Problem for the Primitive Mirror Channel}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The far-field spectral splitting is already fixed by the canonical Callias pair.
What remains is to determine whether the actual global defect solution matches onto the asymptotic decaying sectors with nonzero primitive overlap.

Thus the chirality problem is now a finite radial matching problem.

\subsection{1. Primitive channel and asymptotic splitting}

Take the primitive channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3.
\]
For the canonical Callias Higgs field
\[
\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf1_3),
\]
the asymptotic internal bundle splits as
\[
\mathbb C^3=\operatorname{im}P\oplus\ker P,
\]
with asymptotic decay scales
\[
2|\mu| \quad\text{on }\operatorname{im}P,
\qquad
|\mu| \quad\text{on }\ker P.
\]

Decompose the mirror modes as
\[
\psi_a^{L,R}=z\,\ell_a^{L,R}+\eta_a^{L,R},
\qquad
\eta_a^{L,R}\in\ker P.
\]

Then the primitive overlap density is
\[
\kappa(r)=2A(r)-B(r),
\]
with
\[
A(r)=\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle z\ell_a^R,\Gamma_\chi(z\ell_a^L)\rangle\,d\Omega_r,
\]
\[
B(r)=\sum_{a=1}^2\int_{S_r^2}
\langle \eta_a^R,\Gamma_\chi\eta_a^L\rangle\,d\Omega_r.
\]

\subsection{2. Radial reduction of the actual defect PDE}

Let the actual microscopic defect Dirac-type system be reduced, after angular decomposition, to a first-order radial system
\begin{equation}
\frac{d}{dr}Y(r)=\mathcal M(r)\,Y(r),
\label{eq:radial_system}
\end{equation}
where
\[
Y(r)\in\mathbb C^{N}
\]
collects the line and doublet amplitudes of the left/right mirror sector.

Write
\[
Y(r)=
\begin{pmatrix}
Y_{\mathrm{line}}(r)\\
Y_{\mathrm{dbl}}(r)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
corresponding asymptotically to \(\operatorname{im}P\) and \(\ker P\).

\subsection{3. Core data}

Near the regular defect core \(r=0\), choose the regular basis of solutions
\begin{equation}
Y^{(1)}_{\mathrm{core}}(r),\dots,Y^{(m)}_{\mathrm{core}}(r),
\label{eq:core_basis}
\end{equation}
so the general regular solution is
\begin{equation}
Y_{\mathrm{core}}(r;u)=\sum_{\alpha=1}^{m}u_\alpha Y^{(\alpha)}_{\mathrm{core}}(r).
\label{eq:core_general}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Far-field decaying basis}

At \(r\to\infty\), the asymptotic system diagonalizes into decaying modes of the form
\begin{equation}
Y^{(1)}_{\infty}(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r}v^{(1)}_{\mathrm{line}},
\qquad
\dots,
\qquad
Y^{(p)}_{\infty}(r)\sim e^{-2|\mu|r}v^{(p)}_{\mathrm{line}},
\label{eq:line_far_basis}
\end{equation}
for the line sector, and
\begin{equation}
Y^{(p+1)}_{\infty}(r)\sim e^{-|\mu|r}v^{(p+1)}_{\mathrm{dbl}},
\qquad
\dots,
\qquad
Y^{(q)}_{\infty}(r)\sim e^{-|\mu|r}v^{(q)}_{\mathrm{dbl}},
\label{eq:dbl_far_basis}
\end{equation}
for the doublet sector.

Thus the general \(L^2\)-admissible far-field solution is
\begin{equation}
Y_{\infty}(r;\alpha,\beta)
=
\sum_{s=1}^{p}\alpha_s Y^{(s)}_{\infty}(r)
+
\sum_{t=p+1}^{q}\beta_t Y^{(t)}_{\infty}(r).
\label{eq:far_general}
\end{equation}

The line amplitudes \(\alpha\) determine \(a_\infty\), and the doublet amplitudes \(\beta\) determine \(b_\infty\).

\subsection{5. Matching matrix}

Fix a large radius \(R\) in the overlap region where both the numerical/core integration and the asymptotic basis are valid.
Matching requires
\begin{equation}
Y_{\mathrm{core}}(R;u)=Y_{\infty}(R;\alpha,\beta).
\label{eq:matching_eq}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{match}}(R)
\begin{pmatrix}
u\\ -\alpha\\ -\beta
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
\label{eq:matching_matrix}
\end{equation}

So the existence of an admissible mirror mode is the finite-dimensional kernel condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ker \mathcal M_{\mathrm{match}}(R)\neq\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:kernel_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Extraction of \(a_\infty\) and \(b_\infty\)}

Given one nontrivial matched solution \((u,\alpha,\beta)\in\ker\mathcal M_{\mathrm{match}}(R)\), define
\begin{equation}
a_\infty=\mathfrak a(\alpha),
\qquad
b_\infty=\mathfrak b(\beta),
\label{eq:a_b_extract}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathfrak a,\mathfrak b\) are the primitive line and doublet sesquilinear pairings induced by \(\Gamma_\chi\).

Then the sharpened far-field sufficient criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathfrak a(\alpha),\mathfrak b(\beta))\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
\kappa(r)\not\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\text{full mirror lifting.}
}
\label{eq:final_matching_criterion}
\end{equation}

\subsection{7. Honest remaining microscopic task}

Therefore the remaining chirality problem is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit evaluation of:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the regular core basis \(Y^{(\alpha)}_{\mathrm{core}}\),
\item the decaying far-field basis \(Y^{(s)}_{\infty}\),
\item the matching matrix \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{match}}(R)\),
\item the primitive pairings \(\mathfrak a(\alpha)\), \(\mathfrak b(\beta)\).
\end{enumerate}

Once one matched solution yields
\[
(\mathfrak a(\alpha),\mathfrak b(\beta))\neq(0,0),
\]
the dynamical chirality closure is complete.

\section{Generic Dynamical Closure of Chirality Protection}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At the current stage, the mirror-lifting problem is reduced to the primitive radial overlap density
\[
\kappa(r).
\]
The strongest theorem available from the notes is a generic nonvanishing theorem:
if no additional exact involutive symmetry forces the primitive bilinear to be odd on every sphere,
then \(\kappa\equiv0\) is nongeneric, hence mirror lifting is generic.

\subsection{1. Primitive radial reduction}

The projected mirror block has the exact form
\begin{equation}
\mu(\Xi_f)=c(f)\,\mathbf 1_W,
\qquad
c(f)=\int_0^\infty f(r)\kappa(r)\,dr.
\label{eq:chirality_c_of_f}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa\not\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\exists f:\ c(f)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\mu(\Xi_f)\text{ invertible}
\Longrightarrow
\text{full mirror lifting.}
}
\label{eq:chirality_lifting_chain}
\end{equation}
This part is exact. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{2. Local nonvanishing criterion}

Let
\begin{equation}
\kappa(r)
=
\sum_{a=1}^{2}
\int_{S_r^2}
\left(
2\langle \psi_{a,\parallel}^R,\Gamma_\chi \psi_{a,\parallel}^L\rangle
-
\langle \psi_{a,\perp}^R,\Gamma_\chi \psi_{a,\perp}^L\rangle
\right)
d\Omega_r.
\label{eq:kappa_local}
\end{equation}
If there exists one radius \(r_0>0\) such that this spherical integral is nonzero, then
\[
\kappa(r_0)\neq0,
\]
hence \(\kappa\not\equiv0\). More strongly, if the corresponding primitive bilinear is nonzero at one point in the defect core region, continuity implies nonzero overlap on an interval of radii, so again
\[
\kappa\not\equiv0.
\]
Thus:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one local nonzero primitive bilinear already implies full mirror lifting.}
}
\label{eq:one_point_suffices}
\end{equation}


\subsection{3. Symmetry does not force vanishing}

The \(U(2)\)-equivariance of the primitive channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3
\]
does not imply
\[
\kappa(r)=0.
\]
Indeed, the projected mirror block lies in
\[
\operatorname{End}_{U(2)}(W)\cong \mathbb C,
\]
not in the zero space. Hence symmetry allows exactly one scalar coupling channel, and the primitive channel belongs to it.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(2)\text{ symmetry does not force }\kappa\equiv0.
}
\label{eq:U2_no_force}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{4. The only exact obstruction}

The notes isolate the only exact vanishing mechanism:
an additional involutive symmetry \(\mathcal I\) satisfying
\[
\mathcal I^*P=P,
\qquad
\mathcal I^*\Gamma_\chi=\Gamma_\chi,
\qquad
\mathcal I^*\psi_a^L=-\psi_a^L,
\qquad
\mathcal I^*\psi_a^R=\psi_a^R
\]
for all mirror basis vectors. In that case the primitive bilinear is odd and its spherical integral vanishes on every \(\mathcal I\)-invariant sphere.

Thus:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa\equiv0
\text{ requires an additional exact involutive symmetry of this type.}
}
\label{eq:only_exact_obstruction}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{5. Generic nonvanishing theorem}

The strongest honest genericity theorem in the notes is:

\paragraph{Theorem.}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect stabilizer symmetry is only the standard \(U(2)\) symmetry of the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) defect;
\item the primitive channel
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf1_3
\]
is realized in the natural operator class;
\item there is no additional exact involutive symmetry forcing the primitive mirror bilinear to be odd on every sphere.
\end{enumerate}
Then the condition
\[
\kappa\equiv0
\]
is nongeneric.
Equivalently, for a generic defect-localized radial profile \(f\) in the primitive channel,
\[
c(f)\neq0.
\]

Therefore, under the absence of an accidental exact symmetry,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{mirror lifting is generic in the primitive channel.}
}
\label{eq:generic_lifting}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection{6. Chirality protection after mirror lifting}

The index theorem gives the net chiral asymmetry
\[
n_L-n_R=I.
\]
Index alone does not remove mirror pairs, since
\[
(n_L,n_R)=(I+r,r)
\]
has the same index for any \(r\ge0\). But once the mirror block is invertible, all vectorlike mirror pairs are lifted, leaving exactly the topological chiral sector massless.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{index }+\text{ generic primitive mirror lifting}
\Longrightarrow
\text{protected chiral infrared spectrum of multiplicity }I.
}
\label{eq:chiral_closure_generic}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection{7. Honest final status}

What is now closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item index-protected net chirality,
\item exact finite-dimensional mirror-lifting criterion,
\item reduction to the primitive radial overlap \(\kappa(r)\),
\item proof that \(U(2)\) symmetry does not force \(\kappa\equiv0\),
\item proof that, absent an additional exact involutive symmetry, nonzero primitive overlap is generic.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not absolute:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a full microscopic classification excluding every possible hidden exact involutive symmetry of the TECT defect PDE.}
}
\label{eq:last_not_absolute}
\end{equation}

So the strongest honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{chirality protection is dynamically closed at the generic-theorem level.}
}
\label{eq:generic_theorem_level_closed}
\end{equation}

\section{Microscopic Closure Problem for \(SU(2)_L\) Chirality Selection}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The next unfinished Standard-Model step is not the existence of a \(U(2)\) geometric bundle itself.
That part is already closed.

The genuine remaining electroweak problem is to prove that the emergent \(SU(2)\) connection acts only on the surviving protected left-handed chiral sector after mirror lifting.

\subsection{1. What is already closed}

The internal defect geometry produces the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
Q=(\mathbb Cz)^\perp\to\mathbb{CP}^2,
\end{equation}
with exact local orthonormal-frame redundancy \(U(2)\), and the composite bundle connection
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_\mu=-ie^\dagger\partial_\mu e\in\mathfrak u(2)
\end{equation}
decomposes canonically into
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_\mu=W_\mu+\frac12 B_\mu\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W_\mu\in\mathfrak{su}(2),\quad B_\mu\in\mathfrak u(1).
\end{equation}
So the geometric precursor of electroweak structure is rigorous. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

Moreover, the conditional induced-gauge theorem states that if \(Q\)-charged dynamical fields exist and can be integrated out locally, then the infrared effective action contains
\begin{equation}
-\frac{1}{4g_2^2}F_{\mu\nu}^aF^{a\mu\nu}
-\frac{1}{4g_1^2}G_{\mu\nu}G^{\mu\nu}.
\end{equation}
So induced \(SU(2)\times U(1)\) gauge dynamics is structurally available. 

\subsection{2. What is not yet proved}

The careful theorem audit explicitly says that the following is still open:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{that the }SU(2)\text{ factor acts chirally only on left-handed fermions.}
}
\label{eq:still_open_chiral_SU2}
\end{equation}
This is one of the precise items listed as not yet proved by the current electroweak derivation. 

\subsection{3. Correct formulation of the missing input}

The notes isolate the missing weak input as a preserved rank-two residual internal subbundle
\begin{equation}
\mathcal E_W\to \Sigma
\end{equation}
on which low-energy defect states transform as a doublet
\[
\Psi_W=(\psi_1,\psi_2)^T,
\]
and whose induced connection is traceless and non-Abelian, hence \(\mathfrak{su}(2)\)-valued. 

So the correct microscopic problem is not to invent \(SU(2)\) from nothing, but to prove that the physically realized weak doublet subbundle sits inside the surviving chiral sector and not inside a vectorlike doubled sector.

\subsection{4. Reduction after mirror lifting}

Let the defect zero-mode space decompose as
\begin{equation}
Z_L=Z_{\mathrm{top}}\oplus Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^L,
\qquad
Z_R=Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^R.
\end{equation}
If the mirror block is invertible, then all vectorlike mirror pairs are lifted and only
\[
Z_{\mathrm{top}}\subset \mathcal H_L
\]
remains massless. This part is already rigorously reduced at the mirror-lifting level. 

Hence, after mirror lifting, the weak chirality-selection problem reduces to the following finite inclusion test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_W \subset Z_{\mathrm{top}}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\mathcal E_W\cap Z_R=0.
}
\label{eq:EW_in_left_only}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at projector level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{Z_{\mathrm{top}}}\mathcal E_W=\mathcal E_W,
\qquad
\Pi_{Z_R}\mathcal E_W=0.
}
\label{eq:EW_projector_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Operator form of the same test}

Let \(W_\mu\) denote the emergent weak connection on the low-energy bundle.
Then microscopic \(SU(2)_L\) chirality selection is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_R\,W_\mu\,P_R = 0,
\qquad
P_R\,W_\mu\,P_L = 0,
\qquad
P_L\,W_\mu\,P_L \neq 0
}
\label{eq:operator_chiral_SU2}
\end{equation}
on the massless protected sector after mirror lifting, where \(P_L\) projects to the surviving protected left-handed bundle and \(P_R\) to the right-handed sector.

Thus the open problem is a finite bundle/representation projection audit.

\subsection{6. Strongest honest theorem now available}

The strongest honest electroweak statement currently justified by the notes is:

\paragraph{Theorem (current honest \(SU(2)\)-chirality reduction).}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the rank-two bundle \(Q\to\mathbb{CP}^2\) and its \(U(2)\) connection are realized;
\item a preserved rank-two weak subbundle \(\mathcal E_W\) exists in the defect zero-mode bundle;
\item mirror lifting removes the full vectorlike sector.
\end{enumerate}
Then the remaining microscopic problem of proving \(SU(2)_L\) rather than vectorlike \(SU(2)\) is exactly the finite projection test
\[
\mathcal E_W\subset Z_{\mathrm{top}},
\qquad
\mathcal E_W\cap Z_R=0.
\]

In other words, the weak chirality question is reduced to locating the weak doublet bundle inside the chiral zero-mode decomposition.

\subsection{7. What comes after this}

Only after \eqref{eq:EW_projector_test} is closed does it make sense to move to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) hypercharge }U(1)_Y\text{ embedding},
\qquad
\text{(ii) anomaly cancellation}.
}
\end{equation}
The careful notes explicitly list all three as still open at the complete electroweak level. 

\section{Final Summary}

The next unfinished Standard-Model step is not geometric \(U(2)\) emergence.
That part is already rigorous.

The true remaining electroweak problem is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the emergent }SU(2)\text{ weak connection acts only on the protected left-handed sector.}
}
\]

After mirror lifting, this is equivalent to the finite bundle projection test

\boxed{
\mathcal E_W \subset Z_{\mathrm{top}},
\qquad
\mathcal E_W\cap Z_R=0.

So the next real calculation is:

\text{compute the projection of the weak rank-two bundle into the chiral zero-mode decomposition of the actual defect PDE.}
}

\section{The Next Actual Open: Microscopic Closure of \(SU(2)_L\) Chirality Selection}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The geometric \(U(2)\) precursor is already available from the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) defect bundle.
The real unfinished electroweak problem is not the existence of a weak bundle, but whether that weak bundle sits entirely inside the surviving chiral left-handed sector.

\subsection{1. What is already closed}

The internal defect geometry provides the rank-two Hermitian bundle
\begin{equation}
Q=(\mathbb Cz)^\perp \to \mathbb{CP}^2,
\end{equation}
with local orthonormal-frame redundancy \(U(2)\). Thus local sections of \(Q\) transform in the fundamental representation of the local \(U(2)\) frame bundle. This part is already proved or provable in the current framework. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Moreover, under the hypotheses of the Weak Bundle Emergence Theorem, there exists a smooth rank-two subbundle
\begin{equation}
\mathcal E_W\subset \mathcal E_0
\end{equation}
carrying a natural \(\mathfrak{su}(2)\)-valued Berry connection
\begin{equation}
W_\mu = W_\mu^i \tau^i.
\end{equation}
So a weak \(SU(2)\) sector is conditionally available. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{2. What is still not proved}

The precise unresolved statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{these }Q\text{-valued modes are exactly the Standard Model chiral electroweak doublets.}
}
\label{eq:A7_open}
\end{equation}
This remains explicitly unproved in the current audit, and even the existence of the relevant zero modes is fully proved only in model operators, not yet from the full TECT PDE. 

Therefore the next real task is not to claim electroweak closure, but to prove that the emergent weak bundle is carried by the surviving protected chiral sector.

\subsection{3. Reduction after mirror lifting}

Let the defect zero-mode space decompose as
\begin{equation}
Z_L = Z_{\mathrm{top}}\oplus Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^L,
\qquad
Z_R = Z_{\mathrm{mir}}^R.
\end{equation}
If the mirror block has full rank, then all vectorlike mirror pairs are lifted and only
\[
Z_{\mathrm{top}}\subset Z_L
\]
remains massless. This is already the exact consequence of the mirror-lifting theorem. 

Hence the \(SU(2)_L\) chirality-selection problem reduces to the finite inclusion test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_W \subset Z_{\mathrm{top}},
\qquad
\mathcal E_W \cap Z_R = 0.
}
\label{eq:EW_finite_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Operator form of the same test}

Let \(P_L\) denote the projector onto the protected left-handed massless sector \(Z_{\mathrm{top}}\), and \(P_R\) the projector onto the right-handed sector.
Then the statement that the emergent weak connection is genuinely \(SU(2)_L\) is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_R W_\mu P_R = 0,
\qquad
P_R W_\mu P_L = 0,
\qquad
P_L W_\mu P_L \neq 0.
}
\label{eq:SU2L_operator_test}
\end{equation}
This is the sharp finite projector test that must be checked microscopically.

\subsection{5. Relation to the current Standard-Model theorem}

The current TECT Standard-Model master theorem assumes, among other things:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a preserved rank-two weak subbundle \(\mathcal E_W\),
\item nonzero net chirality with mirror lifting,
\item a chiral matter-bundle decomposition into Standard-Model multiplets.
\end{enumerate}
Therefore the step from geometric \(U(2)\) to genuine \(SU(2)_L\) is still an input to that theorem, not yet a derived consequence. 

\subsection{6. Immediate next executable step}

The next nonredundant microscopic calculation is therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{project the weak rank-two bundle } \mathcal E_W
\text{ into the chiral zero-mode decomposition of the actual defect PDE.}
}
\label{eq:next_exec}
\end{equation}
Operationally:
\begin{enumerate}
\item solve or isolate the protected chiral zero-mode space \(Z_{\mathrm{top}}\),
\item identify the candidate weak doublet bundle \(\mathcal E_W\),
\item compute the bundle/projector overlaps
\[
\Pi_{Z_{\mathrm{top}}}\mathcal E_W,
\qquad
\Pi_{Z_R}\mathcal E_W,
\]
\item verify \eqref{eq:EW_finite_test} or equivalently \eqref{eq:SU2L_operator_test}.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The next actual unfinished Standard-Model step is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the emergent weak rank-two bundle }\mathcal E_W\text{ is contained entirely in the protected left-handed sector.}
}
\]

At present:
\begin{itemize}
\item geometric \(U(2)\) emergence is closed,
\item weak-bundle emergence is conditional but available,
\item mirror lifting is generically closed at theorem level,
\item the identification of the weak bundle with Standard-Model chiral doublets is still open.
\end{itemize}

So the correct next finite test is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_W \subset Z_{\mathrm{top}},
\qquad
\mathcal E_W\cap Z_R=0,
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\boxed{
P_R W_\mu P_R=0,\qquad P_R W_\mu P_L=0,\qquad P_L W_\mu P_L\neq0.
}
\]
Only after this is closed does it make sense to move to hypercharge embedding and anomaly cancellation.
