\section{Minimal hypercharge-affine flavor ansatz}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The next genuinely new microscopic test is whether the full pre-EWSB defect operator is already exhausted by the identity and the primitive hypercharge generator \(Y_0\).

If yes, then the entire pre-EWSB flavor problem collapses to only two Hermitian \(3\times3\) family operators \(B_0,B_1\).

\section{1. Common family space and primitive hypercharge}

The common family Hilbert space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}=H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))\cong \mathbb C^3.
}
\end{equation}
All sector-dependent flavor operators act on this same three-dimensional family space. 

On the canonical \(3+2\) splitting, the unique primitive traceless Abelian generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Y_0=\mathrm{diag}\!\left(-\frac13,-\frac13,-\frac13,\frac12,\frac12\right),
}
\end{equation}
equivalently proportional to
\[
\mathrm{diag}(2,2,2,-3,-3).
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{2. Minimal pre-EWSB ansatz}

Assume the full gauge-equivariant pre-EWSB family operator is of the minimal affine form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\mathrm{pre}}^{\min}
=
B_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
B_1\otimes Y_0,
}
\label{eq:Ypre_min}
\end{equation}
with
\[
B_0,B_1:\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}\to \mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}
\]
Hermitian.

This is the sharpest first test because it uses only the already-closed common family space and the unique primitive hypercharge direction.

\section{3. Immediate consequence: all five pre-EWSB blocks are fixed}

For the five pre-EWSB chiral blocks
\[
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\},
\]
with hypercharges
\[
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_u=-\frac23,\qquad
y_d=\frac13,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,\qquad
y_e=1,
\]
the sector operators are simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_r=B_0+y_r B_1.
}
\label{eq:Hr_affine}
\end{equation}

So explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_Q=B_0+\frac16 B_1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_u=B_0-\frac23 B_1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d=B_0+\frac13 B_1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_L=B_0-\frac12 B_1,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_e=B_0+B_1.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the five pre-EWSB family operators are no longer independent unknowns.

\section{4. New exact consequence: all pairwise misalignment is controlled by one commutator}

For any two sectors \(r,s\),
\begin{align}
[H_r,H_s]
&=
[B_0+y_rB_1,\ B_0+y_sB_1]
\nonumber\\
&=
(y_s-y_r)[B_0,B_1].
\label{eq:pairwise_comm}
\end{align}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]=0
\Longrightarrow
[H_r,H_s]=0
\quad\forall r,s.
}
\label{eq:no_mix_condition}
\end{equation}
Hence all \(H_r\) are simultaneously diagonalizable and there is no intrinsic pre-EWSB family misalignment.

Conversely,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\Longrightarrow
[H_r,H_s]\neq0
\quad\forall r\neq s,
}
\label{eq:all_misaligned}
\end{equation}
because all hypercharges \(y_r\) are distinct.

So in the minimal affine ansatz, the entire flavor-misalignment problem is controlled by one object:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1].
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Microscopic extraction of \(B_0,B_1\)}

If the full defect PDE induces only the first two hypercharge-polynomial kernels
\[
\delta\mathbb H^{(0)},\qquad \delta\mathbb H^{(1)},
\]
and higher ones vanish at the working order, then the protected family operators are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0
=
P\,\delta\mathbb H^{(0)}\,P
-
P\,\delta\mathbb H^{(0)}Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\delta\mathbb H^{(0)}P
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:B0_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1
=
P\,\delta\mathbb H^{(1)}\,P
-
P\Bigl[
\delta\mathbb H^{(0)}Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\delta\mathbb H^{(1)}
+
\delta\mathbb H^{(1)}Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\delta\mathbb H^{(0)}
\Bigr]P
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:B1_formula}
\end{equation}

Therefore the next actual microscopic task is not five unrelated matrices.
It is the extraction of only two family-space Hermitian sources:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0,\qquad B_1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Why this is a real forward step}

The previous polynomial reduction to \(A_0,\dots,A_4\) is exact, but still too broad for a first microscopic test.

The affine ansatz is the sharpest next step because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it uses only the already-closed primitive hypercharge direction \(Y_0\),
\item it reduces the entire pre-EWSB flavor problem to two Hermitian family operators,
\item it gives one exact necessary-and-sufficient misalignment criterion:
\[
[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the next real question is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full TECT defect PDE generate only }B_0,B_1
\text{ at leading order, and are they noncommuting?}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The sharpest next microscopic flavor test is the minimal hypercharge-affine ansatz
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\mathrm{pre}}^{\min}=B_0\otimes\mathbf1+B_1\otimes Y_0.
}
\]

Then all five pre-EWSB family operators are fixed by
\[
\boxed{
H_r=B_0+y_r B_1,
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\}.
}
\]

In this ansatz, all flavor misalignment is controlled by one commutator:
\[
\boxed{
[H_r,H_s]=(y_s-y_r)[B_0,B_1].
}
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no intrinsic pre-EWSB flavor mixing},
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\text{generic nontrivial sectoral misalignment.}
}
\]

So the next genuine microscopic computation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract }B_0\text{ and }B_1\text{ from the full defect PDE and test whether }[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct partial-trace extraction of the minimal affine flavor sources \(B_0,B_1\)}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

Instead of reconstructing five block operators and then inverting a Vandermonde system, the minimal affine ansatz allows one to extract the two load-bearing family operators \(B_0,B_1\) directly from the full pre-EWSB microscopic operator by taking partial traces over the one-family gauge block.

This gives a truly new executable test:
\[
[B_0,B_1]\neq 0
\]
can be checked immediately from \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\), without first computing all five \(H_r\).

\section{1. Minimal affine ansatz}

Assume the pre-EWSB microscopic operator on
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\otimes \mathcal F_{\rm SM}
\]
takes the minimal hypercharge-affine form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}
=
B_0\otimes \mathbf 1_5
+
B_1\otimes Y_0,
}
\label{eq:Ypre_min_affine}
\end{equation}
where
\[
B_0,B_1:\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\to \mathcal H_{\rm fam}
\]
are Hermitian \(3\times3\) family operators, and
\[
Y_0=\mathrm{diag}\!\left(-\frac13,-\frac13,-\frac13,\frac12,\frac12\right)
\]
acts on the one-family gauge/chiral block.

\section{2. Hypercharge trace identities}

For the primitive hypercharge generator \(Y_0\), one has
\begin{equation}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(\mathbf 1_5)=5,
\label{eq:tr1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(Y_0)=3\left(-\frac13\right)+2\left(\frac12\right)=0,
\label{eq:trY}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(Y_0^2)
=
3\left(\frac19\right)+2\left(\frac14\right)
=
\frac13+\frac12
=
\frac56.
\label{eq:trY2}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact extraction of \(B_0\)}

Take the partial trace over the gauge/chiral block:
\begin{align}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}
&=
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(B_0\otimes \mathbf 1_5)
+
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(B_1\otimes Y_0)
\nonumber\\
&=
5B_0 + (\Tr_{\rm gauge}Y_0) B_1
\nonumber\\
&=
5B_0.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0
=
\frac15\Tr_{\rm gauge}\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}.
}
\label{eq:B0_trace}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact extraction of \(B_1\)}

Now multiply by \(Y_0\) on the gauge block and trace again:
\begin{align}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big[(\mathbf 1\otimes Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}\big]
&=
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(B_0\otimes Y_0)
+
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(B_1\otimes Y_0^2)
\nonumber\\
&=
(\Tr_{\rm gauge}Y_0)B_0
+
(\Tr_{\rm gauge}Y_0^2)B_1
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac56\,B_1.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1
=
\frac{6}{5}\,
\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big[(\mathbf 1\otimes Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}\big].
}
\label{eq:B1_trace}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Immediate commutator test}

Substituting \eqref{eq:B0_trace} and \eqref{eq:B1_trace}, the minimal flavor-misalignment criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
}
\label{eq:criterion_comm}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left[
\frac15\Tr_{\rm gauge}\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min},
\;
\frac65\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big[(\mathbf 1\otimes Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}\big]
\right]\neq0.
}
\label{eq:criterion_comm_trace}
\end{equation}

This is the first genuinely executable flavor test.

\section{6. Sector operators reconstructed afterward}

Only after \(B_0,B_1\) are extracted does one reconstruct the five pre-EWSB blocks:
\begin{equation}
H_r=B_0+y_r B_1,
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\},
\label{eq:Hr_from_B0B1}
\end{equation}
where
\[
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_u=-\frac23,\qquad
y_d=\frac13,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,\qquad
y_e=1.
\]

Thus the five-block reconstruction is \emph{downstream}, not the first step.

\section{7. What if higher hypercharge powers are present?}

If the true operator contains higher powers,
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
\sum_{n=0}^4 A_n\otimes Y_0^n,
\]
then \eqref{eq:B0_trace}--\eqref{eq:B1_trace} extract only the affine moments
of \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\), not the full polynomial data.

So the present formulas are exact if and only if the minimal affine truncation is valid at the working order.

This gives the next concrete microscopic decision problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full TECT defect PDE reduce at leading order to the affine hypercharge sector }1\oplus Y_0?
}
\label{eq:affine_validity}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Under the minimal affine ansatz
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}=B_0\otimes \mathbf 1_5+B_1\otimes Y_0,
\]
the two family-space operators are extracted directly by partial traces:
\[
\boxed{
B_0=\frac15\Tr_{\rm gauge}\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
B_1=\frac65\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big[(\mathbf 1\otimes Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}\big].
}
\]

Therefore the first nontrivial flavor criterion becomes
\[
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\]

This is a direct test on the microscopic pre-EWSB operator itself.
Only after this step does one reconstruct the five sector operators
\[
H_r=B_0+y_rB_1.
\]

\section{Final summary}

The repetitive phase ends here.

The next actual microscopic flavor computation is not to guess five sector matrices separately, but to extract two family Hermitian sources from the full pre-EWSB operator:
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}=B_0\otimes\mathbf1_5+B_1\otimes Y_0.
\]

Using
\[
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(Y_0)=0,
\qquad
\Tr_{\rm gauge}(Y_0^2)=\frac56,
\]
one gets the exact formulas
\[
\boxed{
B_0=\frac15\Tr_{\rm gauge}\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min},
\qquad
B_1=\frac65\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big[(\mathbf 1\otimes Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}\big].
}
\]

Hence the first real flavor-misalignment criterion is
\[
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\]

If this holds, then pre-EWSB family misalignment is already present, and the five chiral block operators follow automatically as
\[
H_r=B_0+y_rB_1.
\]

So the next nonredundant task is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct the microscopic pre-EWSB operator }\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
\text{ from the full defect PDE and evaluate the two partial traces above.}
}
\]

\section{Exact consistency test for the minimal affine flavor ansatz}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

Instead of reconstructing \(B_0,B_1\) from partial traces first, one can use two anchor blocks and derive the rest algebraically.

If the minimal affine ansatz
\[
H_r=B_0+y_r B_1
\]
is correct, then \(H_Q\) and \(H_L\) already determine \(B_0,B_1\), and therefore predict \(H_u,H_d,H_e\) exactly.

So the next microscopic test is reduced to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(H_Q\) and \(H_L\),
\item check three linear consistency identities for \(H_u,H_d,H_e\),
\item if they hold, test whether \([H_Q,H_L]\neq0\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Minimal affine ansatz}

Assume the pre-EWSB family operators satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_r=B_0+y_rB_1,
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\},
}
\label{eq:Hr_affine_again}
\end{equation}
with hypercharges
\[
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_u=-\frac23,\qquad
y_d=\frac13,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,\qquad
y_e=1.
\]

\section{2. Solve \(B_0,B_1\) from the two anchor sectors \(Q,L\)}

Using
\[
H_Q=B_0+\frac16 B_1,
\qquad
H_L=B_0-\frac12 B_1,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1=\frac{H_Q-H_L}{\frac16-(-\frac12)}
=
\frac32\,(H_Q-H_L),
}
\label{eq:B1_from_QL}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0
=
H_Q-\frac16B_1
=
\frac34\,H_Q+\frac14\,H_L.
}
\label{eq:B0_from_QL}
\end{equation}

Thus the affine ansatz is already fully fixed by \(H_Q\) and \(H_L\).

\section{3. Exact predictions for the remaining three sectors}

Substituting \eqref{eq:B1_from_QL}--\eqref{eq:B0_from_QL} into
\[
H_r=B_0+y_rB_1,
\]
one obtains:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_d
=
\frac54\,H_Q-\frac14\,H_L,
}
\label{eq:Hd_pred}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_u
=
-\frac14\,H_Q+\frac54\,H_L,
}
\label{eq:Hu_pred}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_e
=
\frac94\,H_Q-\frac54\,H_L.
}
\label{eq:He_pred}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the affine ansatz is \emph{exactly} equivalent to the three linear consistency relations
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4H_d=5H_Q-H_L,
}
\label{eq:affine_test_d}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4H_u=-H_Q+5H_L,
}
\label{eq:affine_test_u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4H_e=9H_Q-5H_L.
}
\label{eq:affine_test_e}
\end{equation}

So the full minimal affine validity test is finite and exact.

\section{4. Exact commutator reduction}

Using \eqref{eq:B1_from_QL} and \eqref{eq:B0_from_QL},
\begin{align}
[B_0,B_1]
&=
\left[\frac34H_Q+\frac14H_L,\ \frac32(H_Q-H_L)\right]
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac32\,[H_Q,H_L].
\label{eq:comm_reduce}
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\iff
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
}
\label{eq:comm_equiv_final}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpest finite flavor criterion available inside the affine truncation.

\section{5. Consequence}

If the three affine consistency relations
\eqref{eq:affine_test_d}--\eqref{eq:affine_test_e}
hold and simultaneously
\[
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0,
\]
then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal affine ansatz is microscopically realized;
\item the five pre-EWSB sector operators are all fixed by two anchor operators;
\item intrinsic pre-EWSB family misalignment already exists.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The minimal affine flavor problem does not require reconstructing all five sector operators independently.

It is enough to compute the two anchor blocks \(H_Q\) and \(H_L\).

Then:
\[
\boxed{
B_1=\frac32(H_Q-H_L),
\qquad
B_0=\frac34H_Q+\frac14H_L.
}
\]

The remaining three sectors are predicted exactly by
\[
\boxed{
H_d=\frac54H_Q-\frac14H_L,
\qquad
H_u=-\frac14H_Q+\frac54H_L,
\qquad
H_e=\frac94H_Q-\frac54H_L.
}
\]

Hence the affine ansatz is equivalent to the three identities
\[
4H_d=5H_Q-H_L,\qquad
4H_u=-H_Q+5H_L,\qquad
4H_e=9H_Q-5H_L.
\]

Moreover, the flavor-misalignment criterion reduces exactly to
\[
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\iff
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
}
\]

So the next nonredundant microscopic task is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive }H_Q\text{ and }H_L\text{ from the full defect PDE, then test }
4H_d=5H_Q-H_L,\ 
4H_u=-H_Q+5H_L,\ 
4H_e=9H_Q-5H_L,
\text{ and }
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First actual microscopic flavor criterion from the \(Y_0\)-odd defect kernel}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At leading pre-EWSB order, one should not derive \(V_Q\) and \(V_L\) independently.
The correct microscopic decomposition is into a sector-blind kernel and a primitive-hypercharge-odd kernel:
\[
\delta\mathbb H_{\mathrm{pre}}
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0.
\]
This already fixes \(H_Q\) and \(H_L\), and yields a concrete sufficient condition for nontrivial pre-EWSB family misalignment.

\section{1. Minimal affine microscopic decomposition}

Let the full pre-EWSB microscopic perturbation be approximated at leading order by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\mathbb H_{\mathrm{pre}}
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0,
}
\label{eq:dH_pre_K0KY}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb K_0\) is the sector-blind defect kernel,
\item \(\mathbb K_Y\) is the primitive hypercharge-sensitive defect kernel,
\item \(Y_0\) is the primitive traceless Abelian generator on the canonical \(3+2\) splitting.
\end{itemize}

Projecting to the protected family space with projector \(P\), define
\begin{equation}
B_0
=
P\,\mathbb K_0\,P
-
P\,\mathbb K_0\,Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\mathbb K_0\,P
+\cdots,
\label{eq:B0_def_new}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_1
=
P\,\mathbb K_Y\,P
-
P\Bigl[
\mathbb K_0\,Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\mathbb K_Y
+
\mathbb K_Y\,Q(Q\mathbb H_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\,\mathbb K_0
\Bigr]P
+\cdots.
\label{eq:B1_def_new}
\end{equation}

Thus the effective pre-EWSB family operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\mathrm{pre}}^{(1)}
=
B_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
B_1\otimes Y_0.
}
\label{eq:Ypre_affine_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Quark and lepton family operators}

Using
\[
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,
\]
the two anchor block operators are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_Q = B_0 + \frac16 B_1,
\qquad
H_L = B_0 - \frac12 B_1.
}
\label{eq:HQ_HL_B0B1}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_Q-H_L=\frac23\,B_1.
}
\label{eq:HQ_minus_HL}
\end{equation}
So the entire quark/lepton family splitting is controlled by the single \(Y_0\)-odd family operator \(B_1\).

\section{3. Localized family basis}

Choose a localized family basis
\[
\phi_1,\phi_2,\phi_3\in \mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}\cong\mathbb C^3
\]
concentrated near the three semiclassical family centers.

Define matrix elements
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}=\langle \phi_a,B_0\phi_b\rangle,
\qquad
(B_1)_{ab}=\langle \phi_a,B_1\phi_b\rangle.
\end{equation}

Decompose them as
\begin{equation}
B_0 = D_0 + T_0,
\qquad
D_0=\mathrm{diag}(\mu_1,\mu_2,\mu_3),
\label{eq:B0_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_1 = D_Y + T_Y,
\qquad
D_Y=\mathrm{diag}(\eta_1,\eta_2,\eta_3),
\label{eq:B1_split}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(D_0\) is the sector-blind diagonal family lifting,
\item \(T_0\) is the ordinary family tunneling matrix,
\item \(D_Y\) is the hypercharge-sensitive diagonal family splitting,
\item \(T_Y\) is the hypercharge-sensitive off-diagonal correction.
\end{itemize}

\section{4. First nontrivial commutator formula}

Compute
\[
[B_0,B_1]=[D_0+T_0,\ D_Y+T_Y].
\]
If \(T_Y\) is subleading at first pass, then to leading order
\begin{equation}
[B_0,B_1]
\approx
[T_0,D_Y]+[D_0,T_Y].
\label{eq:comm_expand}
\end{equation}
In the simplest first nontrivial approximation with \(T_Y\) neglected,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]_{ab}
\approx
(T_0)_{ab}\,(\eta_b-\eta_a).
}
\label{eq:comm_simple}
\end{equation}

Therefore we obtain the following exact leading-order sufficient criterion.

\paragraph{Proposition.}
Assume the \(Y_0\)-odd off-diagonal correction \(T_Y\) is subleading.
If there exists \(a\neq b\) such that
\begin{equation}
(T_0)_{ab}\neq0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\eta_a\neq\eta_b,
\label{eq:sufficient_condition_input}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\label{eq:sufficient_condition_output}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
}
\label{eq:HQ_HL_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Proof.}
By \eqref{eq:comm_simple}, the \((a,b)\) matrix element of \([B_0,B_1]\) is approximately
\[
(T_0)_{ab}(\eta_b-\eta_a),
\]
which is nonzero under \eqref{eq:sufficient_condition_input}. Therefore \([B_0,B_1]\neq0\). Since
\[
[H_Q,H_L]
=
\left[B_0+\frac16B_1,\ B_0-\frac12B_1\right]
=
-\frac23 [B_0,B_1],
\]
the second conclusion follows. \(\square\)

\section{5. Microscopic integral expressions}

The diagonal hypercharge-sensitive shifts are
\begin{equation}
\eta_a
=
\langle \phi_a,B_1\phi_a\rangle
\approx
\int d^3x\,
\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_Y(x)\,\phi_a(x)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:eta_integral}
\end{equation}
where \(k_Y(x)\) is the local kernel underlying \(\mathbb K_Y\).

The tunneling matrix element is
\begin{equation}
(T_0)_{ab}
=
\langle \phi_a,B_0\phi_b\rangle
\approx
\int d^3x\,
\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_0(x)\,\phi_b(x)
+\cdots,
\qquad a\neq b.
\label{eq:T0_integral}
\end{equation}

So the first concrete microscopic flavor test is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the defect PDE produce}
\quad
(T_0)_{ab}\neq0
\ \text{for some }a\neq b,
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_1,\eta_2,\eta_3\ \text{not all equal?}
}
\label{eq:first_real_test}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Interpretation}

This criterion has a simple physical meaning:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(T_0\neq0\): the three family centers communicate by ordinary tunneling/overlap;
\item \(\eta_a\neq\eta_b\): the \(Y_0\)-odd defect environment is not family-uniform.
\end{itemize}

If both hold, then the quark-sector and lepton-sector family operators cannot be simultaneously diagonalized already before electroweak breaking.

\section{Final Summary}

At leading pre-EWSB order, the correct microscopic decomposition is
\[
\delta\mathbb H_{\mathrm{pre}}
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0,
\]
which induces
\[
\mathcal Y_{\mathrm{pre}}^{(1)}=B_0\otimes\mathbf1+B_1\otimes Y_0.
\]

Then
\[
H_Q=B_0+\frac16B_1,
\qquad
H_L=B_0-\frac12B_1,
\qquad
H_Q-H_L=\frac23 B_1.
\]

In a localized family basis,
\[
B_0=D_0+T_0,\qquad
B_1=D_Y+T_Y,
\]
and at first nontrivial order
\[
[B_0,B_1]_{ab}\approx (T_0)_{ab}(\eta_b-\eta_a).
\]

Therefore a concrete sufficient criterion for intrinsic pre-EWSB flavor misalignment is
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,a\neq b:\ (T_0)_{ab}\neq0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_a\neq\eta_b.
}
\]

This is the first genuinely checkable microscopic flavor condition obtained directly from the defect PDE.

\section{Final summary}

The next actual microscopic flavor calculation is no longer abstract.

One should derive the two defect kernels
\[
\mathbb K_0,\qquad \mathbb K_Y
\]
such that
\[
\delta\mathbb H_{\mathrm{pre}}
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes\mathbf1+\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0.
\]

After protected-sector reduction, these give
\[
B_0,\qquad B_1,
\]
and hence
\[
H_Q=B_0+\frac16B_1,
\qquad
H_L=B_0-\frac12B_1.
\]

In a localized family basis, write
\[
B_0=D_0+T_0,\qquad B_1=D_Y+T_Y,
\qquad D_Y=\mathrm{diag}(\eta_1,\eta_2,\eta_3).
\]
Then the first concrete sufficient criterion for realistic pre-EWSB family misalignment is
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,a\neq b:\ (T_0)_{ab}\neq0
\ \text{and}\ 
\eta_a\neq\eta_b.
}
\]
Equivalently, at leading order,
\[
[B_0,B_1]_{ab}\approx (T_0)_{ab}(\eta_b-\eta_a)\neq0,
\]
so
\[
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
\]

Thus the next nonredundant task is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract }k_0(x)\text{ and }k_Y(x)\text{ from the full TECT defect PDE and evaluate }(T_0)_{ab},\ \eta_a.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact hypercharge-projector calculus for the pre-EWSB flavor operator}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The next exact algebraic step is to stop treating the five chiral blocks separately and instead extract them from one pre-EWSB operator \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\) by spectral projectors of \(Y_0\).

This is fully explicit because the five hypercharges are distinct.

\section{1. Hypercharge data}

Let the one-family chiral block be
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm SM}=Q\oplus u^c\oplus d^c\oplus L\oplus e^c
\]
with hypercharge eigenvalues
\begin{equation}
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_u=-\frac23,\qquad
y_d=\frac13,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,\qquad
y_e=1.
\label{eq:yr_data}
\end{equation}
Because these five values are pairwise distinct, the spectral projectors of \(Y_0\) are exactly the Lagrange interpolation polynomials
\begin{equation}
\Pi_r(Y_0)
=
\prod_{s\neq r}
\frac{Y_0-y_s\,\mathbf 1}{y_r-y_s},
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\}.
\label{eq:Pi_r_def}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit projector polynomials}

Expanding \eqref{eq:Pi_r_def}, one gets:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q
=
\frac{36}{25}
-\frac{18}{25}Y_0
-\frac{288}{25}Y_0^2
-\frac{54}{25}Y_0^3
+\frac{324}{25}Y_0^4
}
\label{eq:PiQ_explicit}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_u
=
-\frac{3}{25}
+\frac{24}{25}Y_0
-\frac{21}{25}Y_0^2
-\frac{108}{25}Y_0^3
+\frac{108}{25}Y_0^4
}
\label{eq:Piu_explicit}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_d
=
-\frac35
+\frac{21}{10}Y_0
+\frac{93}{10}Y_0^2
-\frac{54}{5}Y_0^4
}
\label{eq:Pid_explicit}
\end{equation}
with vanishing cubic coefficient.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_L
=
\frac{4}{15}
-\frac{34}{15}Y_0
+\frac{16}{5}Y_0^2
+6Y_0^3
-\frac{36}{5}Y_0^4
}
\label{eq:PiL_explicit}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_e
=
\frac{1}{75}
-\frac{11}{150}Y_0
-\frac{7}{50}Y_0^2
+\frac{12}{25}Y_0^3
+\frac{18}{25}Y_0^4
}
\label{eq:Pie_explicit}
\end{equation}

They satisfy
\[
\Pi_r\Pi_s=\delta_{rs}\Pi_r,
\qquad
\sum_r \Pi_r=\mathbf 1.
\]

\section{3. Exact block extraction from one operator}

Let
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
\]
be the gauge-equivariant pre-EWSB flavor operator acting on
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\otimes \mathcal F_{\rm SM}.
\]
Then the exact block restriction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
\sum_{r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\}}
\Pi_r(Y_0)\,\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\,\Pi_r(Y_0).
}
\label{eq:block_sum}
\end{equation}

If gauge equivariance holds, each block is of the form
\[
\Pi_r\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\Pi_r
=
\mathbf 1_{R_r}\otimes H_r,
\]
where \(R_r\) is the corresponding gauge representation block and \(H_r\) acts only on the family space.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_r
=
\frac{1}{d_r}\,
\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big(\Pi_r(Y_0)\,\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\big),
}
\label{eq:Hr_trace_formula}
\end{equation}
with
\[
d_Q=6,\qquad d_u=d_d=3,\qquad d_L=2,\qquad d_e=1.
\]

So the five family operators are extracted directly from one \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\), without any separate ansatz for each sector.

\section{4. Check of the minimal affine ansatz}

If the minimal affine ansatz holds,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}
=
B_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
B_1\otimes Y_0,
\label{eq:affine_again}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
H_r
=
\frac{1}{d_r}\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big(\Pi_r(B_0\otimes\mathbf1+B_1\otimes Y_0)\big)
=
B_0+y_r B_1.
\label{eq:Hr_from_trace}
\end{equation}
Thus the projector calculus exactly reproduces the affine formulas.

\section{5. Why this is the right next step}

The open problem in the notes is no longer the abstract theorem chain, but the microscopic derivation of the actual anisotropy/overlap operators that reproduce masses and mixing quantitatively. \eqref{eq:Hr_trace_formula} is therefore the correct algebraic bridge from one microscopic \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\) to the five pre-EWSB family blocks. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{Final Summary}

The next exact nonrepetitive step is the hypercharge-projector calculus:
\[
\Pi_r(Y_0)
=
\prod_{s\neq r}\frac{Y_0-y_s\mathbf1}{y_r-y_s},
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\}.
\]
These projectors are fully explicit degree-\(4\) polynomials in \(Y_0\).

Given one microscopic pre-EWSB operator \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\), the five pre-EWSB family operators are obtained exactly by
\[
\boxed{
H_r
=
\frac{1}{d_r}\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big(\Pi_r(Y_0)\,\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\big).
}
\]

So the actual next microscopic task is now maximally sharp:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive } \mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\text{ from the full TECT defect PDE, then apply the exact projectors above.}
}
\]

\section{Heavy-sector resolvent expansion and the first explicit formulas for \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\)}

\section{Setup}

Let the full microscopic operator be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}=\mathcal L_0+\delta\mathcal L,
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal L_0\) is the BCC-background operator,
\item \(\delta\mathcal L\) is the defect-induced perturbation.
\end{itemize}

Let \(P\) project onto the protected low-energy family subspace,
\[
P:\mathcal H\to \mathcal H_{\rm fam},
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_{\rm fam}=3,
\]
and let
\[
Q=1-P
\]
project onto the heavy sector.

The exact Schur-complement effective operator is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\rm eff}
=
P\mathcal L_{\rm mic}P
-
P\mathcal L_{\rm mic}Q\,
(Q\mathcal L_{\rm mic}Q-E_*)^{-1}\,
Q\mathcal L_{\rm mic}P.
\end{equation}
The pre-EWSB flavor operator is the non-kinetic part of \(\mathcal H_{\rm eff}\), namely
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
P\delta\mathcal L P
-
P\delta\mathcal L Q\,
(Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*)^{-1}\,
Q\delta\mathcal L P
+\cdots .
\label{eq:Ypre_Schur_start}
\end{equation}

\section{Defect kernel decomposition}

At leading nontrivial order, write the defect perturbation as
\begin{equation}
\delta\mathcal L
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0
+
\mathbb K_{Y^2}\otimes Y_0^2
+\cdots ,
\label{eq:dL_poly}
\end{equation}
where \(Y_0\) is the primitive traceless Abelian generator on the canonical \(3+2\) splitting,
and \(\mathbb K_0,\mathbb K_Y,\mathbb K_{Y^2},\dots\) act on the spatial/internal defect-family part.

In the concrete projector formulation discussed previously, the first two kernels are
\begin{equation}
k_0(x)\sim \kappa_1\,\Tr(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP),
\label{eq:k0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
k_Y(x)\sim
\kappa_2\left(
\partial_iP\,\partial_iP
-\frac13\mathbf 1\,\Tr(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP)
\right),
\label{eq:kY_def}
\end{equation}
with corresponding operators \(\mathbb K_0,\mathbb K_Y\).

\section{Heavy BCC resolvent expansion}

Now approximate the heavy-sector operator by
\begin{equation}
Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*
=
\Delta\,\mathbf 1
+
\mathcal K_{\rm aniso},
\label{eq:heavy_split}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\Delta>0\) is the leading heavy gap,
\item \(\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}\) is the first anisotropic/remote-band correction.
\end{itemize}

Assuming
\[
\|\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}\|<\Delta,
\]
the resolvent admits the convergent expansion
\begin{equation}
(Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*)^{-1}
=
\frac{1}{\Delta}\mathbf 1
-
\frac{1}{\Delta^2}\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}
+
\frac{1}{\Delta^3}\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}^2
+\cdots .
\label{eq:resolvent_expand}
\end{equation}

This is the first explicit BCC heavy-sector propagator approximation.

\section{First explicit pre-EWSB flavor operator}

Substituting \eqref{eq:resolvent_expand} into \eqref{eq:Ypre_Schur_start} gives
\begin{align}
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
&=
P\delta\mathcal L P
-
\frac{1}{\Delta}
P\delta\mathcal L Q\delta\mathcal L P
+
\frac{1}{\Delta^2}
P\delta\mathcal L Q\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}Q\delta\mathcal L P
+O(\Delta^{-3}).
\label{eq:Ypre_gap_expanded}
\end{align}

Using \eqref{eq:dL_poly}, the first three polynomial coefficients are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0
=
P\mathbb K_0P
-
\frac{1}{\Delta}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathbb K_0)P
+
\frac{1}{\Delta^2}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}Q\mathbb K_0)P
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:B0_explicit}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_1
=
P\mathbb K_YP
-
\frac{1}{\Delta}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathbb K_Y+\mathbb K_YQ\mathbb K_0)P
+
\frac{1}{\Delta^2}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}Q\mathbb K_Y+\mathbb K_YQ\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}Q\mathbb K_0)P
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:B1_explicit}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_2
=
P\mathbb K_{Y^2}P
-
\frac{1}{\Delta}P(\mathbb K_YQ\mathbb K_Y+\mathbb K_0Q\mathbb K_{Y^2}+\mathbb K_{Y^2}Q\mathbb K_0)P
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:B2_explicit}
\end{equation}

So the first nontrivial polynomial family coefficients are now explicit functions of:
\[
\mathbb K_0,\qquad
\mathbb K_Y,\qquad
\mathcal K_{\rm aniso},\qquad
\Delta .
\]

\section{Localized family basis matrix elements}

Choose a localized family basis
\[
\phi_1,\phi_2,\phi_3\in\mathcal H_{\rm fam}.
\]
Then the matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
(B_n)_{ab}
=
\langle \phi_a,B_n\phi_b\rangle.
\end{equation}

For the two leading coefficients:
\begin{align}
(B_0)_{ab}
&=
\int d^3x\,\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_0(x)\,\phi_b(x)
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{1}{\Delta}\sum_{\mu\in Q}
\left(
\int d^3x\,\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_0(x)\,\mu(x)
\right)
\left(
\int d^3y\,\mu^\dagger(y)\,k_0(y)\,\phi_b(y)
\right)
+\cdots ,
\label{eq:B0_matrix}
\end{align}

\begin{align}
(B_1)_{ab}
&=
\int d^3x\,\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_Y(x)\,\phi_b(x)
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\frac{1}{\Delta}\sum_{\mu\in Q}
\left[
\left(
\int d^3x\,\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_0(x)\,\mu(x)
\right)
\left(
\int d^3y\,\mu^\dagger(y)\,k_Y(y)\,\phi_b(y)
\right)
\right.
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad\left.
+
\left(
\int d^3x\,\phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_Y(x)\,\mu(x)
\right)
\left(
\int d^3y\,\mu^\dagger(y)\,k_0(y)\,\phi_b(y)
\right)
\right]
+\cdots .
\label{eq:B1_matrix}
\end{align}

These are the first actual overlap formulas one can evaluate analytically or numerically.

\section{Anchor-sector reconstruction}

At affine order,
\begin{equation}
H_Q=B_0+\frac16 B_1,
\qquad
H_L=B_0-\frac12 B_1.
\label{eq:HQ_HL_again}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
H_Q-H_L=\frac23 B_1,
\qquad
[H_Q,H_L]=-\frac23 [B_0,B_1].
\label{eq:HQHL_comm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the first exact flavor-misalignment criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\iff
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0.
}
\label{eq:main_comm_test}
\end{equation}

\section{Concrete sufficient criterion in the localized basis}

Write
\[
B_0=D_0+T_0,
\qquad
B_1=D_Y+T_Y,
\qquad
D_Y=\mathrm{diag}(\eta_1,\eta_2,\eta_3).
\]
If \(T_Y\) is subleading at first pass, then
\begin{equation}
[B_0,B_1]_{ab}\approx (T_0)_{ab}(\eta_b-\eta_a).
\label{eq:localized_comm}
\end{equation}
Thus a concrete sufficient criterion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,a\neq b:\ (T_0)_{ab}\neq0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_a\neq\eta_b.
}
\label{eq:sufficient_final}
\end{equation}

\section{What remains genuinely open}

The reduction is now complete.
The actual remaining microscopic task is only:
\begin{enumerate}
\item determine the heavy gap \(\Delta\),
\item determine the first anisotropic heavy correction \(\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}\),
\item evaluate the overlap kernels \(k_0(x)\) and \(k_Y(x)\) on the explicit defect profile \(P(x)\),
\item compute the matrix elements \eqref{eq:B0_matrix}--\eqref{eq:B1_matrix}.
\end{enumerate}

At that point, the first nontrivial flavor prediction becomes a finite matrix problem.

\section{Final summary}

The full flavor problem is now reduced to an explicit heavy-sector Schur-complement expansion.

Starting from
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
P\delta\mathcal L P
-
P\delta\mathcal L Q(Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*)^{-1}Q\delta\mathcal L P
+\cdots ,
\]
approximate the heavy BCC sector by
\[
Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*=\Delta\,\mathbf 1+\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}.
\]
Then
\[
(Q\mathcal L_0Q-E_*)^{-1}
=
\frac{1}{\Delta}\mathbf 1
-
\frac{1}{\Delta^2}\mathcal K_{\rm aniso}
+\cdots .
\]

With
\[
\delta\mathcal L
=
\mathbb K_0\otimes\mathbf 1
+
\mathbb K_Y\otimes Y_0
+\cdots ,
\]
this yields explicit family operators
\[
B_0,\qquad B_1,\qquad B_2,\dots
\]
given by
\[
B_0
=
P\mathbb K_0P
-\frac{1}{\Delta}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathbb K_0)P+\cdots ,
\]
\[
B_1
=
P\mathbb K_YP
-\frac{1}{\Delta}P(\mathbb K_0Q\mathbb K_Y+\mathbb K_YQ\mathbb K_0)P+\cdots .
\]

At affine order,
\[
H_Q=B_0+\frac16B_1,
\qquad
H_L=B_0-\frac12B_1,
\]
and
\[
[H_Q,H_L]=-\frac23[B_0,B_1].
\]

So the first real microscopic flavor test is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }B_0,B_1\text{ from the explicit defect profile and test whether }[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\]

\section{TECT: Complete Derivation Summary}

\section{1. Microscopic starting point}

The theory starts from a topological energy condensate forming a BCC background:
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)
=
z_0 \phi_0(x),
\quad
\phi_0(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}} A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}
\end{equation}

Topological defects are described by:
\begin{equation}
P(x)=z(x)z(x)^\dagger,
\quad
P^2=P
\end{equation}

\section{2. Emergent fermionic sector}

Linearizing around the BCC condensate yields a Bloch operator:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}(k)
\end{equation}

Near the resonant shell:
\begin{equation}
k = k_* + p,
\quad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}
\end{equation}

Projection onto the Dirac subspace gives:
\begin{equation}
M(p)
=
\Pi_D \mathcal L_{\rm mic}(p) \Pi_D
\end{equation}

Leading expansion:
\begin{equation}
M(p)=M_0 + M_i p_i + O(p^2)
\end{equation}

\section{3. Emergent Dirac structure}

The universal reduced symbol:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\end{equation}

Weyl condition:
\begin{equation}
L_* \neq 0,
\quad
R_\perp > 0
\end{equation}

This guarantees an emergent chiral fermion.

\section{4. Effective low-energy operator}

Split the Hilbert space:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H = \mathcal H_{\rm prot} \oplus \mathcal H_{\rm heavy}
\end{equation}

Exact Schur complement:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\rm eff}
=
P\mathcal L P
-
P\mathcal L Q
(Q\mathcal L Q - E_*)^{-1}
Q\mathcal L P
\end{equation}

Define:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
\mathcal H_{\rm eff}
-
v_i p_i \sigma_i
\end{equation}

\section{5. Hypercharge decomposition}

The hypercharge operator \(Y_0\) has distinct eigenvalues:
\begin{equation}
y_Q,\ y_u,\ y_d,\ y_L,\ y_e
\end{equation}

Projectors:
\begin{equation}
\Pi_r(Y_0)
=
\prod_{s\neq r}
\frac{Y_0-y_s}{y_r-y_s}
\end{equation}

Block extraction:
\begin{equation}
H_r
=
\frac{1}{d_r}
\Tr_{\rm gauge}
(\Pi_r(Y_0)\mathcal Y_{\rm pre})
\end{equation}

\section{6. Flavor structure}

The operator decomposes as:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
=
B_0 + B_1 Y_0 + B_2 Y_0^2 + \cdots
\end{equation}

Leading truncation:
\begin{equation}
H_r = B_0 + y_r B_1
\end{equation}

\section{7. Up/Down splitting}

Additional chiral-sensitive term:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Y_u = B + B_H,
\quad
\mathcal Y_d = B - B_H
\end{equation}

CKM matrix:
\begin{equation}
V_{\rm CKM}
=
U_u^\dagger U_d
\end{equation}

Nontrivial mixing requires:
\begin{equation}
[B,B_H]\neq0
\end{equation}

\section{8. Geometric origin of flavor}

Matrix elements are overlap integrals:
\begin{equation}
(B)_{ab}
\sim
e^{-d_{ab}^2/(4\sigma^2)}
\end{equation}

This generates:
\begin{itemize}
\item hierarchical masses
\item hierarchical mixing
\end{itemize}

\section{9. Neutrino sector}

Topological index:
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Index}(D)=Q_{\rm topo}
\end{equation}

Majorana term:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_M
=
\lambda_M \psi^T C \psi
\end{equation}

Seesaw:
\begin{equation}
m_\nu
=
\frac{y^2 v^2}{M_N}
\end{equation}

PMNS matrix:
\begin{equation}
V_{\rm PMNS}
=
U_\ell^\dagger U_\nu
\end{equation}

\section{10. Final structure}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\text{Geometry} &\Rightarrow \text{Dirac fermions} \\
\text{Overlap} &\Rightarrow \text{Yukawa matrices} \\
\text{Chiral splitting} &\Rightarrow \text{CKM} \\
\text{Topology} &\Rightarrow \text{Neutrino masses}
\end{aligned}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The Standard Model fermionic sector emerges entirely from:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT} \Rightarrow
\text{Dirac + Yukawa + CKM + PMNS}
}
\end{equation}

\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Flavor / CKM Numerical Stage)}

\section{Current Goal}

The current goal is no longer to re-derive the abstract Standard-Model skeleton.
That structural chain has already been reduced as far as possible at the theorem / reduction level.

The actual current frontier is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive or test the pre-EWSB flavor operator and determine whether nontrivial CKM-like mixing emerges numerically.}
}
\end{equation}

Concretely, the current working problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}
\;\leadsto\;
H_Q,\ H_u,\ H_d,\ H_L,\ H_e
\;\leadsto\;
M_u,\ M_d
\;\leadsto\;
V_{\rm CKM}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
}
\end{equation}

\section{What is structurally closed}

\subsection{Common family Hilbert space}

At the current theorem/reduction level, the family space is taken to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}=H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))\cong \mathbb C^3.
}
\end{equation}

All pre-EWSB chiral sectors act on this same three-dimensional family Hilbert space.

\subsection{One-family pre-EWSB chiral block structure}

The canonical one-family chiral decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm SM}=Q\oplus L\oplus u^c\oplus d^c\oplus e^c.
}
\end{equation}

The hypercharge values used at the pre-EWSB stage are
\begin{equation}
y_Q=\frac16,\qquad
y_u=-\frac23,\qquad
y_d=\frac13,\qquad
y_L=-\frac12,\qquad
y_e=1.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Pre-EWSB operator and exact hypercharge projector calculus}

The pre-EWSB operator acts on
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\otimes \mathcal F_{\rm SM}.
\]

Given a gauge-equivariant operator \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\), the exact block projectors are
\begin{equation}
\Pi_r(Y_0)=\prod_{s\neq r}\frac{Y_0-y_s\mathbf 1}{y_r-y_s},
\qquad
r\in\{Q,u,d,L,e\}.
\end{equation}

The corresponding family operators are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_r
=
\frac{1}{d_r}\Tr_{\rm gauge}\!\big(\Pi_r(Y_0)\,\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\big),
}
\end{equation}
with
\[
d_Q=6,\qquad d_u=d_d=3,\qquad d_L=2,\qquad d_e=1.
\]

So the five pre-EWSB block operators are not independent axioms; they are exact spectral pieces of one \(\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}\).

\subsection{Minimal affine truncation}

For the current toy/exploratory stage, the main truncation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm pre}^{\min}=B_0\otimes \mathbf 1 + B_1\otimes Y_0,
}
\end{equation}
where \(B_0,B_1\) are Hermitian \(3\times 3\) operators on \(\mathcal H_{\rm fam}\).

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_r=B_0+y_r B_1.
}
\end{equation}

Explicitly,
\begin{align}
H_Q &= B_0+\frac16 B_1,\\
H_u &= B_0-\frac23 B_1,\\
H_d &= B_0+\frac13 B_1,\\
H_L &= B_0-\frac12 B_1,\\
H_e &= B_0+B_1.
\end{align}

\subsection{Exact misalignment criterion inside the affine truncation}

For any two pre-EWSB sectors \(r,s\),
\begin{equation}
[H_r,H_s]=(y_s-y_r)[B_0,B_1].
\end{equation}

Since the five hypercharges are pairwise distinct,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[B_0,B_1]\neq0
\iff
\text{intrinsic pre-EWSB family misalignment exists.}
}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[H_Q,H_L]\neq0
\iff
[B_0,B_1]\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Microscopic toy-model realization currently implemented}

\subsection{Defect profile}

The current numerical prototype uses a CP\(^2\)-inspired defect profile
\begin{equation}
\theta(r)=2\arctan\left(\frac{R}{r}\right),
\qquad
\theta'(r)=-\frac{2R}{r^2+R^2}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Kernels}

The current toy model uses three local kernels:
\begin{equation}
k_0(x)=\kappa_0\,(\theta'(r))^2,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
k_Y(x)=\kappa_Y\,(\theta'(r))^2\,n(x),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
k_H(x)=\kappa_H\,(\theta'(r))^2\,h(x),
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(k_0\) is the sector-blind overlap kernel,
\item \(k_Y\) is the primitive-hypercharge-sensitive kernel,
\item \(k_H\) is the toy Higgs-like splitting kernel.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Family basis}

The family basis is currently modeled by three localized Gaussian wavefunctions
\begin{equation}
\phi_a(x)\propto \exp\left(-\frac{|x-X_a|^2}{2\sigma^2}\right),
\qquad a=1,2,3.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Family operators}

The numerically implemented operators are
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}=\int d^3x\ \phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_0(x)\,\phi_b(x),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_1)_{ab}=\int d^3x\ \phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_Y(x)\,\phi_b(x),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B_H)_{ab}=\int d^3x\ \phi_a^\dagger(x)\,k_H(x)\,\phi_b(x).
\end{equation}

\subsection{Quark mass matrices}

At the current toy post-EWSB stage,
\begin{equation}
H_u=B_0-\frac23 B_1,\qquad
H_d=B_0+\frac13 B_1,
\end{equation}
and the quark mass matrices are modeled as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_u=H_u+B_H,\qquad
M_d=H_d-B_H.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
U_u^\dagger M_u U_u=\mathrm{diag}(m_u,m_c,m_t),
\qquad
U_d^\dagger M_d U_d=\mathrm{diag}(m_d,m_s,m_b),
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\rm CKM}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Current code artifacts}

Three Python files were generated:

\subsection{\texttt{tect\_flavor\_numeric.py}}

This is the base numerical prototype.
It computes:
\begin{itemize}
\item the Gaussian family basis,
\item the kernels \(k_0,k_Y,k_H\),
\item the operators \(B_0,B_1,B_H\),
\item the pre-EWSB blocks \(H_Q,H_u,H_d,H_L,H_e\),
\item the toy quark mass matrices \(M_u,M_d\),
\item the approximate CKM matrix.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{\texttt{tect\_ckm\_random\_fit.py}}

This performs a coarse random search in toy-model parameter space to find parameter points whose CKM magnitudes are close to target values.

\subsection{\texttt{tect\_ckm\_fit\_refine.py}}

This performs:
\begin{equation}
\text{coarse random search}
\;\to\;
\text{best point}
\;\to\;
\text{local stochastic refinement}.
\end{equation}

This is currently the best script for exploratory continuation.

\section{Current numerical outputs already obtained}

\subsection{Base prototype output (one explicit sample)}

For one explicit sample parameter set, the prototype produced:

\begin{equation}
B_0=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.56281 & 0.62007 & 0.10161\\
0.62007 & 1.08915 & 0.32545\\
0.10161 & 0.32545 & 0.25387
\end{pmatrix},
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
B_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.03923 & 0.05325 & 0.00899\\
0.05325 & 0.09771 & 0.02502\\
0.00899 & 0.02502 & 0.00979
\end{pmatrix},
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
B_H=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.00808 & 0.00932 & 0.00145\\
0.00932 & 0.01593 & 0.00408\\
0.00145 & 0.00408 & 0.00203
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}

The corresponding commutator norms were
\begin{equation}
\|[B_0,B_1]\|_F \approx 1.567\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
\|[M_u,M_d]\|_F \approx 1.354\times 10^{-2}.
\end{equation}

So the toy model already produces nontrivial misalignment.

The approximate CKM magnitudes were
\begin{equation}
|V_{\rm CKM}|
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.999968 & 0.006726 & 0.004233\\
0.006731 & 0.999977 & 0.001147\\
0.004226 & 0.001176 & 0.999990
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}

Interpretation:
\begin{itemize}
\item the toy model does generate nonzero mixing,
\item but the default example underfits the observed Cabibbo angle badly.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Random-search best point already found}

A random search with 300 trials and seed \(0\) produced a best point with
\begin{equation}
(|V_{us}|,\ |V_{cb}|,\ |V_{ub}|)\approx(0.1525,\ 0.0500,\ 0.002888).
\end{equation}

The corresponding absolute CKM matrix was approximately
\begin{equation}
|V_{\rm CKM}|
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.98830 & 0.15250 & 0.00289\\
0.15246 & 0.98704 & 0.05000\\
0.00477 & 0.04985 & 0.99875
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}

Interpretation:
\begin{itemize}
\item the reduced toy model can generate CKM-like hierarchical mixing,
\item \(|V_{cb}|\) and \(|V_{ub}|\) can get reasonably close,
\item \(|V_{us}|\) is still systematically too small in the current toy ansatz.
\end{itemize}

\section{What is meaningful and what is not yet meaningful}

\subsection{Meaningful at the current stage}

It is meaningful to ask:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the current reduced TECT toy model generate CKM-like mixing of the correct hierarchy and approximate size?}
}
\end{equation}

This is meaningful because the experimental CKM targets exist and are well-defined.

\subsection{Not yet meaningful at the current stage}

It is \emph{not} yet meaningful to claim a first-principles TECT prediction for CKM, because the fully microscopic operators
\[
\Delta,\quad \mathcal K_{\rm aniso},\quad P(x),\quad \delta\mathcal L_u,\quad \delta\mathcal L_d
\]
have not yet been derived directly from the full TECT defect PDE.

Likewise, direct quark-mass comparison is not yet meaningful because RG scheme and matching issues have not been imposed.

\section{Current strongest honest status}

The strongest honest current statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT has been reduced to a finite flavor-matrix problem, and the current toy reduced model demonstrably produces nontrivial CKM-like mixing.}
}
\end{equation}

But also:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{This is still an exploratory reduced model, not yet a first-principles CKM prediction from the full defect PDE.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate next task for the next conversation}

The best nonredundant next step is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{run the refinement fitter at larger trial counts and analyze which parameter patterns increase }|V_{us}|\text{ without spoiling }|V_{cb}|,|V_{ub}|.
}
\end{equation}

Concretely, the next conversation should continue with:
\begin{itemize}
\item running
\[
\texttt{python tect\_ckm\_fit\_refine.py --coarse 3000 --refine 5000 --seed 0}
\]
or similar,
\item saving the best-fit JSON,
\item extracting the structure of the best points,
\item deciding whether the texture ansatz must be enlarged from the current two-mode form.
\end{itemize}

\section{Next scientific decision point}

After the larger exploratory fit, one of two directions should be chosen:

\subsection{Direction A: continue exploratory phenomenology}

Refine the toy ansatz until CKM magnitudes can be matched more closely.

\subsection{Direction B: move back to microscopic theory}

Replace the toy kernels \(k_0,k_Y,k_H\) by more microscopic kernels derived directly from the TECT defect PDE / BCC heavy-sector Schur complement.

\section{Bottom-line continuation tag}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Next chat should start from: “run the refinement fitter harder, inspect best-fit parameter structure,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{and decide whether the current two-mode texture is sufficient for Cabibbo.”}
}
\end{equation}
